## 10. preposition
**Part of Speech Family:** preposition
**Frequency:** 27490

---
topic: pronouns
pos: pronoun
frequency: 34682
---

# Lesson: Ancient Greek Pronouns  

*Prepared for beginner‑intermediate students of Classical Greek*  

---

## 1. What Are Pronouns?

A **pronoun** (Greek: *ἀντωνυμία*) is a word that stands in for a noun or a noun phrase.  
Pronouns function like nouns in the sense that they are **declined** (change case, number, gender) and they can be the subject, object, or possessive in a clause.  

In Ancient Greek the main groups of pronouns are:

| Group | Typical English counterpart | Greek label |
|-------|----------------------------|-------------|
| Personal | I, you, he/she/it, we, you (pl.) | *προσωπικές* |
| Demonstrative | this, that, these, those | *δείκτες* |
| Relative | who, which, that | *συγγενικές* |
| Interrogative / Indefinite | who?, what?, any, some | *ερωτηματικές / αόριστες* |
| Reflexive | oneself | *αυτοαναφορικές* |
| Possessive | my, your, his, etc. | *κτητικές* |
| Intensive (emphatic) | **himself**, **themselves** | *εντείνουσες* |

All of these pronouns are **substantives** (they belong to the part of speech “noun”) and therefore follow the regular noun declension patterns (first, second, or third declension) with a few irregularities that we will meet below.

---

## 2. Forms and Patterns  

Below are the full paradigms for the most frequently used pronoun families.  
When a pronoun has a **different stem** for the genitive or dative, the table shows the stem in parentheses.

### 2.1 Personal Pronouns  

| Case | 1st sg. (I) | 2nd sg. (you) | 3rd sg. masc. | 3rd sg. fem. | 3rd sg. neut. | 1st pl. (we) | 2nd pl. (you) | 3rd pl. masc. | 3rd pl. fem. | 3rd pl. neut. |
|------|-------------|--------------|---------------|--------------|--------------|--------------|--------------|---------------|--------------|--------------|
| **Nominative** | ἐγώ | σύ | ἐκεῖνος / ὁ (masc.) | ἐκείνη / ἡ (fem.) | ἐκεῖνο / τό (neut.) | ἡμεῖς | ὑμεῖς | οἱ (masc.) | αἱ (fem.) | τὰ (neut.) |
| **Genitive** | (μου) | (σου) | (αὐτοῦ) | (αὐτῆς) | (αὐτοῦ) | (ἡμῶν) | (ὑμῶν) | (αὐτῶν) | (αὐτῶν) | (αὐτῶν) |
| **Dative** | (μοι) | (σοι) | (αὐτῷ) | (αὐτῇ) | (αὐτῷ) | (ἡμῖν) | (ὑμῖν) | (αὐτοῖς) | (αὐταῖς) | (αὐτοῖς) |
| **Accusative** | (με) | (σέ) | (αὐτόν) | (αὐτήν) | (αὐτό) | (ἡμᾶς) | (ὑμᾶς) | (αὐτούς) | (αὐτάς) | (αὐτά) |
| **Vocative** | ὦ ἐγώ | ὦ σύ | — | — | — | ὦ ἡμεῖς | ὦ ὑμεῖς | — | — | — |

*Notes*  

* The enclitic forms in parentheses are the ordinary unstressed forms used after a verb or preposition (e.g., **μου** “my”, **σου** “your”).  
* The demonstrative‑type personal pronouns **ἐγώ, σύ, ἡμεῖς, ὑμεῖς** have a special **strong** form (shown in the nominative) used for emphasis or after the particle **ὦ**.  

---

### 2.2 Demonstrative Pronouns  

Greek has three basic demonstrative stems: **οὗτος** (this, near the speaker), **ἐκεῖνος** (that, far from the speaker), and **ὅδε** (this, near the addressee). The most common textbook paradigm is **οὗτος**; the others follow the same pattern.

| Case | Masculine | Feminine | Neuter |
|------|-----------|----------|--------|
| **Nominative** | οὗτος | αὕτη | τοῦτο |
| **Genitive** | τούτου | ταύτης | τούτου |
| **Dative** | τῷ (τοῦ) | τῇ (ταύ) | τῷ (τοῦ) |
| **Accusative** | τοῦτον | ταύτην | τοῦτο |
| **Vocative** | οὗτε | αὕτη· (rare) | τοῦτο |

*Key points*  

* The **genitive** and **accusative** of neuter are identical to the masculine forms.  
* The **dative** uses the article‑like endings **‑ῳ / ‑ῃ / ‑ῳ** (often written **‑ῳ** for all genders).  

---

### 2.3 Relative Pronoun  

The relative pronoun **ὅς, ἥ, ὅ** (“who, which, that”) is declined like a **third‑declension adjective** but with a special set of endings.

| Case | Masculine | Feminine | Neuter |
|------|-----------|----------|--------|
| **Nominative** | ὅς | ἥ | ὅ |
| **Genitive** | οὗ | ἧς | οὗ |
| **Dative** | ᾧ | ᾗ | ᾧ |
| **Accusative** | ὅν | ἥν | ὅ |
| **Vocative** | — | — | — |

*Important*  

* The relative pronoun **agrees in gender, number, and case** with its antecedent (the noun it refers to).  
* In poetry the **dual** forms (e.g., **οὗ** for neuter dual) may appear, but they are rare in prose.

---

### 2.4 Interrogative Pronoun  

The interrogative pronoun **τίς, τί** (“who?, what?”) follows the same pattern as the relative pronoun.

| Case | Masculine/Feminine | Neuter |
|------|-------------------|--------|
| **Nominative** | τίς | τί |
| **Genitive** | τίνος | τίνος |
| **Dative** | τίνι | τίνι |
| **Accusative** | τίνα | τί |
| **Vocative** | — | — |

*Note*: The interrogative can also appear as **πότε** (when?) and **πῶς** (how?), which are adverbs rather than pronouns.

---

### 2.5 Possessive Pronouns  

Possessive adjectives are formed from the personal pronoun stems plus the endings of the **first‑ and second‑declension adjectives**. The most common forms are:

| Person | Masculine | Feminine | Neuter |
|--------|-----------|----------|--------|
| 1st sg. | ἐμός, ἐμή, ἐμόν | — | — |
| 2nd sg. | σός, σή, σόν | — | — |
| 3rd sg. masc. | αὐτοῦ (gen.) → **αὐτοῦ** (adj. **αὐτοῦ**) – rarely used as adjective; instead we use **αὐτοῦ** as genitive of **αὐτός** |
| 3rd sg. fem. | — | αὐτῆς | — |
| 3rd sg. neut. | — | — | αὐτοῦ |
| 1st pl. | ἡμῶν (gen.) → **ἡμέτερος**, **ἡμετέρα**, **ἡμέτερον** |
| 2nd pl. | ὑμῶν → **ὑμέτερος**, **ὑμετέρα**, **ὑμέτερον** |
| 3rd pl. | αὐτῶν → **αὐτῶν** (gen.) – rarely as adjective; we use **αὐτοῦ** etc. |

*Simplified table for the adjective forms*  

| Person | Masculine | Feminine | Neuter |
|--------|-----------|----------|--------|
| 1st sg. | ἐμός | ἐμή | ἐμόν |
| 2nd sg. | σός | σή | σόν |
| 1st pl. | ἡμέτερος | ἡμετέρα | ἡμέτερον |
| 2nd pl. | ὑμέτερος | ὑμετέρα | ὑμέτερον |

*Key rule*: Possessive adjectives **agree** with the noun they modify in gender, number, and case, just like any other adjective.

---

### 2.6 Reflexive Pronoun  

The reflexive pronoun **ἑαυτός** (“himself, herself, itself, themselves”) is a **first‑person** adjective that behaves like a **third‑declension adjective**.

| Case | Masculine | Feminine | Neuter |
|------|-----------|----------|--------|
| **Nominative** | ἑαυτός | ἑαυτή | ἑαυτό |
| **Genitive** | ἑαυτοῦ | ἑαυτῆς | ἑαυτοῦ |
| **Dative** | ἑαυτῷ | ἑαυτῇ | ἑαυτῷ |
| **Accusative** | ἑαυτόν | ἑαυτήν | ἑαυτό |
| **Vocative** | — | — | — |

*Usage*: The reflexive is used when the subject and object of a verb are the same person or thing (e.g., **ἔλεξεν ἑαυτόν** “he spoke to himself”).

---

### 2.7 Indefinite Pronouns  

Indefinite pronouns have many forms; the most common are **τις, τι, τις, τινα** (someone, something, any). They decline like the interrogative pronoun.

| Case | Masculine/Feminine | Neuter |
|------|-------------------|--------|
| Nominative | τις | τι |
| Genitive | τινός | τινός |
| Dative | τινι | τινι |
| Accusative | τινα | τι |
| Vocative | — | — |

Other indefinite pronouns (e.g., **πᾶς, οὐδείς, ἄλλος**) follow regular adjective or noun declensions and are treated in later chapters.

---

## 3. Key Rules & Common Exceptions  

| Rule | Explanation | Example |
|------|-------------|---------|
| **Agreement** | Pronouns must agree with the noun they replace or modify in **gender, number, case**. | *ὁ ἀνὴρ* → *αὐτός* (masc. nom. sg.) |
| **Enclitic vs. Strong Forms** | Personal pronouns have a **strong** (stressed) form in the nominative (ἐγώ, σύ, ἡμεῖς, ὑμεῖς) and a **weak** enclitic form in other cases (μου, σου, ἡμῶν, ὑμῶν). | *ἔστιν ἐγώ* (strong) vs. *ἔστιν μοι* (enclitic) |
| **Genitive of Possession** | The genitive of a personal pronoun (μου, σου, ἡμῶν, ὑμῶν) can express **possession** without a separate possessive adjective. | *τὸ βιβλίον μου* “my book” |
| **Demonstrative vs. Personal** | Demonstratives (οὗτος, ἐκεῖνος) can function as **personal pronouns** when the referent is clear, especially in narrative. | *οὗτος ἦλθεν* “He (this one) came.” |
| **Relative Pronoun Agreement** | The relative pronoun **always matches the antecedent** in gender, number, and case, **not** the case required by its function in the relative clause. | *ἡ γυνὴ ἣν ἔβλεψα* – “the woman **whom** I saw” (accusative because of the verb *ἔβλεψα*, but the pronoun is feminine singular because the antecedent *γυνή* is feminine). |
| **Interrogative Pronoun Position** | In questions, the interrogative pronoun often appears **

### Exercises

### Exercise Set 1

What are the following prepositions?

1. ἐν (lemma: ἐν)
2. ὡς (lemma: ὡς)
3. ἐς (lemma: εἰς)
4. ἐφ̓ (lemma: ἐπί)
5. ἐκ (lemma: ἐκ)
6. πρὸς (lemma: πρός)
7. καθ̓ (lemma: κατά)
8. περὶ (lemma: περί)
9. ὑφ̓ (lemma: ὑπό)
10. παρὰ (lemma: παρά)
11. μετὰ (lemma: μετά)
12. ἀπὸ (lemma: ἀπό)
13. διὰ (lemma: διά)
14. ἅμα (lemma: ἅμα)
15. ἀμφὶ (lemma: ἀμφί)

### Exercise Set 2

Identify the marked preposition in each sentence and give the case it governs.

1. τῶν δὲ <u>κατὰ</u> τὠυτὸ αἱ γνῶμαι συνεξέπιπτον κελευόντων ἐσδέκεσθαι Τόμυρίν τε καὶ τὸν στρατὸν αὐτῆς <u>ἐς</u> τὴν χώρην. " ὣς φάθ̓, ὁ δ̓ αὖτις ἰὼν <u>κατ̓</u> ἄῤ ἕζετο · τῷ δὲ συβώτης. οὐ δέ νυ σοί περ ἐντρέπεται φίλον ἦτορ ἀνεψιοῦ κταμένοιο;

2. οἳ δ̓ ὅτε δὴ κλισίῃσιν <u>ἐν</u> Ἀτρεΐδαο γένοντο.

3. ἐχθρὰ δέ μοι τοῦ δῶρα, τίω δέ μιν <u>ἐν</u> καρὸς αἴσῃ.

4. οἱ μὲν ἐκήρυσσον, τοὶ δ̓ ἠγείροντο μάλ̓ ὦκα. οἳ δ̓ ἤτοι δακέειν μὲν ἀπετρωπῶντο λεόντων, ἱστάμενοι δὲ μάλ̓ ἐγγὺς ὑλάκτεον <u>ἔκ</u> τ̓ ἀλέοντο.

5. οἳ δ̓ <u>ἐπ̓</u> ὀνείαθ̓ ἑτοῖμα προκείμενα χεῖρας ἴαλλον.

6. οἳ δ̓ <u>ἐπ̓</u> ὀνείαθ̓ ἑτοῖμα προκείμενα χεῖρας ἴαλλον.

7. ἣ δ̓ ἄτη σθεναρή τε καὶ ἀρτίπος, οὕνεκα πάσας πολλὸν ὑπεκπροθέει, φθάνει δέ τε πᾶσαν <u>ἐπ̓</u> αἶαν βλάπτουσ̓ ἀνθρώπους · αἳ δ̓ ἐξακέονται ὀπίσσω.

8. τοῖσι δ̓ ἔπειθ̓ ἥρως Αἰγύπτιος ἦρχ̓ ἀγορεύειν, ὃς δὴ γήραϊ κυφὸς ἔην καὶ μυρία ᾔδη. τῶν δ̓ αἳ μὲν λεπτὰς ὀθόνας ἔχον, οἳ δὲ χιτῶνας εἵατ̓ ἐϋννήτους, ἦκα στίλβοντας ἐλαίῳ · καί ῥ̓ αἳ μὲν καλὰς στεφάνας ἔχον, οἳ δὲ μαχαίρας εἶχον χρυσείας <u>ἐξ</u> ἀργυρέων τελαμώνων.

9. Ἱερώνυμος δ̓ ὁ περιπατητικὸς περισπουδάστους φησὶν γενέσθαι τοὺς τῶν παίδων ἔρωτας ὅτι πολλάκις ἡ τῶν νέων ἀκμὴ καὶ τὸ <u>πρὸς</u> ἀλλήλους ἑταιρικὸν συμφρονῆσαν πολλὰς τυραννίδας καθεῖλεν. Κολοφωνίους ἄνδρας στάσι ἑσσωθέντας καὶ ἐκπεσόντας <u>ἐκ</u> τῆς πατρίδος ὑπεδέξαντο. " τὸν δ̓ ἀπαμειβόμενος προσέφη πολύμητις Ὀδυσσεύς " τοιγὰρ ἐγώ τοι ταῦτα μάλ̓ ἀτρεκέως ἀγορεύσω. ὁ δὲ Βάρκας ὀψὲ μὲν συνῆκε τὴν ἐπίθεσιν τῶν <u>ἐκ</u> τῆς πόλεως <u>διὰ</u> τὴν ἀπόστασιν τῶν στρατοπέδων · οὐδὲ μὴν συνεὶς οὐδ̓ οὕτως κατετάχει <u>πρὸς</u> τὴν βοήθειαν <u>διὰ</u> τὰς μεταξὺ δυσχωρίας. ἠχὴ δ̓ ἀμφοτέρων ἵκετ̓ αἰθέρα καὶ Διὸς αὐγάς.

10. οἳ δ̓ ὡς οὖν εἴδονθ̓ ὅ τ̓ ἄῤ <u>ἐκ</u> Διὸς ἤλυθεν ὄρνις, μᾶλλον <u>ἐπὶ</u> Τρώεσσι θόρον, μνήσαντο δὲ χάρμης.

### Exercise Set 3

State the governed case for each marked preposition and identify its complement.

1. νήποινοί κεν ἔπειτα δόμων <u>ἔντοσθεν</u> ὄλοισθε. ἣ δ̓ ἐκύει φίλον υἱόν, ὃ δ̓ ἕβδομος ἑστήκει μείς · <u>ἐκ</u> δ̓ ἄγαγε πρὸ φόως δὲ καὶ ἠλιτόμηνον ἐόντα, Ἀλκμήνης δ̓ ἀπέπαυσε τόκον, σχέθε δ̓ Εἰλειθυίας.

2. ὣς τὸ μὲν ἐξετέλεσσε καὶ οὐκ ἐθέλουσ̓, <u>ὑπ̓</u> ἀνάγκης. ὣς φάτ̓ Ἀθηναίη, ὃ δ̓ ἐπείθετο, χαῖρε δὲ θυμῷ, στῆ δ̓ ἄῤ <u>ἐπὶ</u> μελίης χαλκογλώχινος ἐρεισθείς.

3. τὴν μὲν γὰρ Ἕλληνὲς ναυτίλλονται πᾶσα καὶ ἡ <u>ἔξω</u> στηλέων θάλασσα ἡ Ἀτλαντὶς καλεομένη καὶ ἡ Ἐρυθρὴ μία ἐοῦσα τυγχάνει. οἱ δ̓ αἶψ̓ εἴσβαινον καὶ <u>ἐπὶ</u> κληῗσι καθῖζον. ὣς εἰπὼν ὄτρυνε μένος καὶ θυμὸν ἑκάστου.

4. αἱ δ̓ ἄμοτον τανύοντο, φέρον δ̓ ἐσθῆτα καὶ αὐτήν, οὐκ οἴην, <u>ἅμα</u> τῇ γε καὶ ἀμφίπολοι κίον ἄλλαι. ἀλλ̓ ἴθι ταῦτα δ̓ ὄπισθεν ἀρεσσόμεθ̓ εἴ τι κακὸν νῦν εἴρηται, τὰ δὲ πάντα θεοὶ μεταμώνια θεῖεν.

5. ἄλλα δ̓ ἀριστήεσσι δίδου γέρα καὶ βασιλεῦσι · τοῖσι μὲν ἔμπεδα κεῖται, ἐμεῦ δ̓ <u>ἀπὸ</u> μούνου Ἀχαιῶν εἵλετ̓, ἔχει δ̓ ἄλοχον θυμαρέα · τῇ παριαύων τερπέσθω.

6. οἱ δὲ προειρημένοι Χαλκιδεῖς <u>παῤ</u> αὑτοῖς φασιν ἁρπασθῆναι τὸν Γανυμήδην <u>ὑπὸ</u> τοῦ Διὸς καὶ τὸν τόπον δεικνύντες Ἁρπάγιον καλοῦσιν, <u>ἐν</u> ᾧ καὶ μυρρίναι διάφοροι πεφύκασιν. οὗτοι δὲ οἱ Αἰολέες χώρην μὲν ἔτυχον κτίσαντες ἀμείνω Ἰώνων, ὡρέων δὲ ἥκουσαν οὐκ ὁμοίως. τίνες ἔμμεναι εὐχετόωντο; οἱ δὲ <u>περὶ</u> τὸν Μάθω κατανοήσαντες τὸν Ἀννίβαν ῥᾳθύμως καὶ κατατεθαρρηκότως ἀναστρεφόμενον, ἐπιθέμενοι τῷ χάρακι πολλοὺς μὲν τῶν Καρχηδονίων ἀπέκτειναν, πάντας δ̓ ἐξέβαλον <u>ἐκ</u> τῆς στρατοπεδείας, ἐκυρίευσαν δὲ καὶ τῆς ἀποσκευῆς ἁπάσης, ἔλαβον δὲ καὶ τὸν στρατηγὸν Ἀννίβαν ζωγρίᾳ. ὣς ἄρα φωνήσας ἡγήσατο · τοὶ δ̓ ἅμ̓ ἕποντο ἠχῇ θεσπεσίῃ, <u>ἐπὶ</u> δ̓ ἴαχε λαὸς ὄπισθεν.

7. ἐπεὶ ὅς τις ἀνὴρ ἀγαθὸς καὶ ἐχέφρων τὴν αὐτοῦ φιλέει καὶ κήδεται, ὡς καὶ ἐγὼ τὴν <u>ἐκ</u> θυμοῦ φίλεον δουρικτητήν περ ἐοῦσαν.

8. ἐπείτε δὲ ἐπεραιώθη τὸν Ἀράξεα, νυκτὸς ἐπελθούσης εἶδε ὄψιν εὕδων <u>ἐν</u> τῶν Μασσαγετέων τῇ χωρῇ τοιήνδε · ἐδόκεε ὁ Κῦρος <u>ἐν</u> τῷ ὕπνῳ ὁρᾶν τῶν Ὑστάσπεος παίδων τὸν πρεσβύτατον ἔχοντα <u>ἐπὶ</u> τῶν ὤμων πτέρυγας καὶ τουτέων τῇ μὲν τὴν Ἀσίην τῇ δὲ τὴν Εὐρώπην ἐπισκιάζειν. πρῆξαι δ̓ ἀργαλέον τι <u>μετὰ</u> πλεόνεσσιν ἐόντα ἄνδρα καὶ ἴφθιμον, ἐπεὶ ἦ πολὺ φέρτεροί εἰσι. μινυνθάδιος γὰρ ἔμελλεν ἔσσεσθ̓ · ἤδη γάρ οἱ ἐπόρνυε μόρσιμον ἦμαρ Παλλὰς Ἀθηναίη <u>ὑπὸ</u> Πηλεΐδαο βίηφιν.

9. τοὶ δ̓ <u>ἐξ</u> ἀγροῖο πόλινδε ὠτρύνοντ̓ Ὀδυσεύς τ̓ ἰέναι καὶ δῖος ὑφορβός. ἀνὴρ δ̓ ὤριστος ὄλωλε Σαρπηδὼν Διὸς υἱός · ὃ δ̓ οὐ οὗ παιδὸς ἀμύνει.

10. σμερδαλέον δὲ μέγ̓ ᾤμωξεν, <u>περὶ</u> δ̓ ἴαχε πέτρη, ἡμεῖς δὲ δείσαντες ἀπεσσύμεθ̓ · αὐτὰρ ὁ μοχλὸν ἐξέρυσ̓ ὀφθαλμοῖο πεφυρμένον αἵματι πολλῷ. τοῦ δ̓ ἤτοι κλέος ἔσται ὅσον τ̓ ἐπικίδναται ἠώς · τοῦ δ̓ ἐπιλήσονται τὸ ἐγὼ καὶ Φοῖβος Ἀπόλλων ἥρῳ Λαομέδοντι πολίσσαμεν ἀθλήσαντε.


#### Answer Key for Exercise Set 1

1. ἐν (lemma: ἐν) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
2. ὡς (lemma: ὡς) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
3. ἐς (lemma: εἰς) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
4. ἐφ̓ (lemma: ἐπί) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
5. ἐκ (lemma: ἐκ) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
6. πρὸς (lemma: πρός) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
7. καθ̓ (lemma: κατά) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
8. περὶ (lemma: περί) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
9. ὑφ̓ (lemma: ὑπό) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
10. παρὰ (lemma: παρά) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
11. μετὰ (lemma: μετά) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
12. ἀπὸ (lemma: ἀπό) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
13. διὰ (lemma: διά) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
14. ἅμα (lemma: ἅμα) -> preposition; governs case: unknown
15. ἀμφὶ (lemma: ἀμφί) -> preposition; governs case: unknown


---

## 11. dative
**Part of Speech Family:** noun/adjective
**Frequency:** 25414

## Introduction to the Dative Case

The dative case marks the indirect object, the recipient, or the “to/for” relation. Its form is created by attaching a case‑ending to the noun’s stem; the shape of that ending depends on the declension to which the noun belongs.

---

### 1. First‑declension (‑ᾱ / ‑η stems)

| Gender           | Singular ending | Example                                     | Plural ending     | Example                                         |
| ---------------- | --------------- | ------------------------------------------- | ----------------- | ----------------------------------------------- |
| Feminine         | ‑ᾱ‑ι / ‑η‑ι     | _γλῶσ‑σῃ_ → **γλῶσῃ** “to/for the tongue”   | ‑α‑ις (or ‑α‑ισι) | _γλῶσ‑σαις_ → **γλώσσαις** “to/for the tongues” |
| Masculine (rare) | ‑ᾱ‑ι            | _νεαν‑ι_ → **νεανί** “to/for the young man” | ‑α‑ις             | _νεαν‑αίς_ → **νεαναίς** “to/for the young men” |

_Morphology_ – The stem ends in a long vowel (‑ᾱ or ‑η). In the singular the long‑i **‑ι** is added directly after that vowel, giving a long‑i ending (‑ᾱι, ‑ηι). In the plural the vowel is followed by **‑α‑ις**, producing a short‑i ending that is pronounced as a single syllable.

---

### 2. Second‑declension (‑ο stems, including “‑ο‑stem” adjectives)

| Gender             | Singular ending | Example                                            | Plural ending | Example                                                  |
| ------------------ | --------------- | -------------------------------------------------- | ------------- | -------------------------------------------------------- |
| Masculine / neuter | ‑ῳ              | _φίλ‑ῳ_ → **τῷ φίλῳ** “to/for the friend”          | ‑οις          | _φίλ‑οις_ → **τοῖς φίλοις** “to/for the friends”         |
| Feminine (‑ος)     | ‑ῳ              | _δίκαι‑ῳ_ → **τῷ δικαίῳ** “to/for the just person” | ‑οις          | _δίκαι‑οις_ → **τοῖς δικαίοις** “to/for the just people” |

_Morphology_ – The stem ends in **‑ο** (or **‑ε** for some neuters). The dative singular adds the long‑i **‑ῳ**, while the plural adds **‑οις**. The original accent of the noun is retained as far as Greek phonological rules allow.

---

### 3. Third‑declension (mixed‑stem nouns)

Because third‑declension stems vary (consonantal, i‑stems, u‑stems, etc.), several patterns occur. The most frequent are:

| Stem type      | Singular ending | Example                                   | Plural ending | Example                                         |
| -------------- | --------------- | ----------------------------------------- | ------------- | ----------------------------------------------- |
| Consonant‑stem | ‑ι              | _πόλε‑ι_ → **τῷ πόλει** “to/for the city” | ‑σι           | _πόλε‑σι_ → **τοῖς πόλεσι** “to/for the cities” |
| i‑stem         | ‑ι              | _γῆ‑ι_ → **τῇ γῇ** “to/for the earth”     | ‑σι           | _γῆ‑σι_ → **τοῖς γῆσι** “to/for the lands”      |
| u‑stem         | ‑ῳ              | _ναῦ‑ῳ_ → **τῷ ναῦῳ** “to/for the ship”   | ‑οις          | _ναῦ‑οις_ → **τοῖς ναῦοις** “to/for the ships”  |

_Morphology_ – The stem may undergo a minor adjustment (often a lengthening or a consonant change) before the dative suffix is attached. The default suffixes are **‑ι** for the singular and **‑σι** for the plural; u‑stems follow the second‑declension pattern **‑ῳ / ‑οις**.

---

### General principles that apply to all declensions

1. **Accent preservation** – The noun’s original accent stays on the same syllable whenever the addition of the dative ending does not force a shift. An acute on the penult of the nominative typically remains on the penult in the dative; an acute on the antepenult may move forward when the ending is added.
2. **Length of the ultima** – Dative endings themselves are long (**‑ῳ, ‑οις**) or short (**‑ι, ‑σι**). This length influences accent placement and the behavior of any following enclitic.
3. **Enclitic interaction** – When a dative form is followed by an enclitic (e.g., the verb _εἰμί_), the enclitic receives no accent if the preceding word ends in a long ultima; otherwise the enclitic may acquire an accent on its final syllable.

---

### Summary of the core endings

| Declension          | Singular ending | Plural ending            |
| ------------------- | --------------- | ------------------------ |
| First               | ‑ᾱ‑ι / ‑η‑ι     | ‑α‑ις                    |
| Second              | ‑ῳ              | ‑οις                     |
| Third (most common) | ‑ι              | ‑σι (u‑stems: ‑ῳ / ‑οις) |

These endings attach directly to the noun’s stem, producing the dative forms that express “to” or “for” the noun in Ancient Greek.


### Exercises

### Exercise Set 1

Which declension do the following words belong to?

1. κἀμοὶ (lemma: ἐγώ)
2. αὐτῷ (lemma: αὐτός)
3. ᾧ (lemma: ὅς)
4. σοι (lemma: σύ)
5. τούτῳ (lemma: οὗτος)
6. τινι (lemma: τις)
7. πάσῃ (lemma: πᾶς)
8. τῇσιδε (lemma: ὅδε)
9. ἀνδρὶ (lemma: ἀνήρ)
10. πολλῷ (lemma: πολύς)
11. ἄλλοις (lemma: ἄλλος)
12. θεοῖς (lemma: θεός)
13. μεγάλῳ (lemma: μέγας)
14. νηὶ (lemma: ναῦς)
15. Διί (lemma: Ζεύς)

### Exercise Set 2

What is the gender, case, and number of the marked words?

1. " ὣς ἔφατ̓ εὐχόμενος, τοῦ δ̓ ἔκλυε Παλλὰς Ἀθήνη. οἳ δ̓ ἄῤ ἔσαν δίδυμοι · ὃ μὲν ἔμπεδον ἡνιόχευεν, ἔμπεδον ἡνιόχεὐ, ὃ δ̓ ἄρα <u>μάστιγι</u> κέλευεν.

2. ὣς φάτο, τοῖσι δὲ <u>πᾶσιν</u> ἑαδότα μῦθον ἔειπεν.

3. οἳ δ̓ ὅτε δὴ <u>κλισίῃσιν</u> ἐν Ἀτρεΐδαο γένοντο.

4. ἐχθρὰ δέ μοι τοῦ δῶρα, τίω δέ μιν ἐν καρὸς <u>αἴσῃ</u>.

5. ὣς ἔφαθ̓, οἳ δ̓ ἄρα πάντες ἀκὴν ἐγένοντο <u>σιωπῇ</u>.

6. τοῖσι δ̓ ἔπειθ̓ ἥρως Αἰγύπτιος ἦρχ̓ ἀγορεύειν, ὃς δὴ <u>γήραϊ</u> κυφὸς ἔην καὶ μυρία ᾔδη. τῶν δ̓ αἳ μὲν λεπτὰς ὀθόνας ἔχον, οἳ δὲ χιτῶνας εἵατ̓ ἐϋννήτους, ἦκα στίλβοντας <u>ἐλαίῳ</u> · καί ῥ̓ αἳ μὲν καλὰς στεφάνας ἔχον, οἳ δὲ μαχαίρας εἶχον χρυσείας ἐξ ἀργυρέων τελαμώνων.

7. οἳ δ̓ ὡς οὖν εἴδονθ̓ ὅ τ̓ ἄῤ ἐκ Διὸς ἤλυθεν ὄρνις, μᾶλλον ἐπὶ <u>Τρώεσσι</u> θόρον, μνήσαντο δὲ χάρμης.

8. τοῦ δ̓ ὠρίνετο θυμὸς ἀκούοντος κακὰ ἔργα, βῆ δ̓ ἰέναι, <u>χροῒ</u> δ̓ ἔντἐ ἐδύσετο παμφανόωντα.

9. δῶκε δὲ <u>Τηλεμάχῳ</u> καλὸν δέπας ἀμφικύπελλον · ὣς δ̓ αὔτως ἠρᾶτο Ὀδυσσῆος φίλος υἱός. τὸν τώ γ̓ ἑσταότες πενθείετον, <u>οὔδεϊ</u> δέ σφι χαῖται ἐρηρέδαται, τὼ δ̓ ἕστατον ἀχνυμένω κῆρ.

10. ὣς τὸ μὲν ἐξετέλεσσε καὶ οὐκ ἐθέλουσ̓, ὑπ̓ ἀνάγκης. ὣς φάτ̓ Ἀθηναίη, ὃ δ̓ ἐπείθετο, χαῖρε δὲ <u>θυμῷ</u>, στῆ δ̓ ἄῤ ἐπὶ μελίης χαλκογλώχινος ἐρεισθείς.

### Exercise Set 3

Translate each sentence and identify the marked noun or adjective.

1. τὴν μὲν γὰρ Ἕλληνὲς ναυτίλλονται πᾶσα καὶ ἡ ἔξω στηλέων θάλασσα ἡ Ἀτλαντὶς καλεομένη καὶ ἡ Ἐρυθρὴ μία ἐοῦσα τυγχάνει. οἱ δ̓ αἶψ̓ εἴσβαινον καὶ ἐπὶ <u>κληῗσι</u> καθῖζον. ὣς εἰπὼν ὄτρυνε μένος καὶ θυμὸν ἑκάστου.

2. ἀλλ̓ ἄγε μοι τὸν ὄνειρον ὑπόκριναι καὶ ἄκουσον. οἳ δὲ τάχα προγένοντο, δύω δ̓ ἅμ̓ ἕποντο νομῆες τερπόμενοι <u>σύριγξι</u> · δόλον δ̓ οὔ τι προνόησαν.

3. ἄλλα δ̓ <u>ἀριστήεσσι</u> δίδου γέρα καὶ <u>βασιλεῦσι</u> · τοῖσι μὲν ἔμπεδα κεῖται, ἐμεῦ δ̓ ἀπὸ μούνου Ἀχαιῶν εἵλετ̓, ἔχει δ̓ ἄλοχον θυμαρέα · τῇ παριαύων τερπέσθω.

4. οἱ δὲ προειρημένοι Χαλκιδεῖς παῤ αὑτοῖς φασιν ἁρπασθῆναι τὸν Γανυμήδην ὑπὸ τοῦ Διὸς καὶ τὸν τόπον δεικνύντες Ἁρπάγιον καλοῦσιν, ἐν ᾧ καὶ μυρρίναι διάφοροι πεφύκασιν. οὗτοι δὲ οἱ Αἰολέες χώρην μὲν ἔτυχον κτίσαντες ἀμείνω Ἰώνων, ὡρέων δὲ ἥκουσαν οὐκ ὁμοίως. τίνες ἔμμεναι εὐχετόωντο; οἱ δὲ περὶ τὸν Μάθω κατανοήσαντες τὸν Ἀννίβαν ῥᾳθύμως καὶ κατατεθαρρηκότως ἀναστρεφόμενον, ἐπιθέμενοι τῷ <u>χάρακι</u> πολλοὺς μὲν τῶν Καρχηδονίων ἀπέκτειναν, πάντας δ̓ ἐξέβαλον ἐκ τῆς στρατοπεδείας, ἐκυρίευσαν δὲ καὶ τῆς ἀποσκευῆς ἁπάσης, ἔλαβον δὲ καὶ τὸν στρατηγὸν Ἀννίβαν ζωγρίᾳ. ὣς ἄρα φωνήσας ἡγήσατο · τοὶ δ̓ ἅμ̓ ἕποντο <u>ἠχῇ</u> <u>θεσπεσίῃ</u>, ἐπὶ δ̓ ἴαχε λαὸς ὄπισθεν.

5. ὣς ὃ μὲν <u>Αἰτωλοῖσιν</u> ἀπήμυνεν κακὸν ἦμαρ εἴξας <u>ᾧ</u> <u>θυμῷ</u> · τῷ δ̓ οὐκέτι δῶρα τέλεσσαν πολλά τε καὶ χαρίεντα, κακὸν δ̓ ἤμυνε καὶ αὔτως.

6. ἐπείτε δὲ ἐπεραιώθη τὸν Ἀράξεα, νυκτὸς ἐπελθούσης εἶδε ὄψιν εὕδων ἐν τῶν Μασσαγετέων τῇ <u>χωρῇ</u> τοιήνδε · ἐδόκεε ὁ Κῦρος ἐν τῷ <u>ὕπνῳ</u> ὁρᾶν τῶν Ὑστάσπεος παίδων τὸν πρεσβύτατον ἔχοντα ἐπὶ τῶν ὤμων πτέρυγας καὶ τουτέων τῇ μὲν τὴν Ἀσίην τῇ δὲ τὴν Εὐρώπην ἐπισκιάζειν. πρῆξαι δ̓ ἀργαλέον τι μετὰ <u>πλεόνεσσιν</u> ἐόντα ἄνδρα καὶ ἴφθιμον, ἐπεὶ ἦ πολὺ φέρτεροί εἰσι. μινυνθάδιος γὰρ ἔμελλεν ἔσσεσθ̓ · ἤδη γάρ οἱ ἐπόρνυε μόρσιμον ἦμαρ Παλλὰς Ἀθηναίη ὑπὸ Πηλεΐδαο <u>βίηφιν</u>.

7. ὣς ἔφαθ̓, αἳ δ̓ ἐπέμυξαν Ἀθηναίη τε καὶ Ἥρη · πλησίαι αἵ γ̓ ἥσθην, κακὰ δὲ <u>Τρώεσσι</u> μεδέσθην.

8. νῦν δ̓ ὅττι ῥυπόω, κακὰ δὲ <u>χροῒ</u> εἵματα εἷμαι, τοὔνεκ̓ ἀτιμάζει με καὶ οὔ πω φησὶ τὸν εἶναι. ἀλλὰ τάχιστα παυώμεσθα μάχης · οἳ δ̓ αὐτοὶ δηριαάσθων.

9. σμερδαλέον δὲ μέγ̓ ᾤμωξεν, περὶ δ̓ ἴαχε πέτρη, ἡμεῖς δὲ δείσαντες ἀπεσσύμεθ̓ · αὐτὰρ ὁ μοχλὸν ἐξέρυσ̓ ὀφθαλμοῖο πεφυρμένον <u>αἵματι</u> <u>πολλῷ</u>. τοῦ δ̓ ἤτοι κλέος ἔσται ὅσον τ̓ ἐπικίδναται ἠώς · τοῦ δ̓ ἐπιλήσονται τὸ ἐγὼ καὶ Φοῖβος Ἀπόλλων <u>ἥρῳ</u> <u>Λαομέδοντι</u> πολίσσαμεν ἀθλήσαντε.

10. " ὣς ἔφατ̓ Ἀντίνοος · ὁ δ̓ ἄῤ οὐκ ἐμπάζετο μύθων. καὶ τὰ μὲν ἂρ <u>σχίζῃσιν</u> <u>ἀφύλλοισιν</u> κατέκαιον, σπλάγχνα δ̓ ἄῤ ἀμπείραντες ὑπείρεχον Ἡφαίστοιο.


#### Answer Key for Exercise Set 1

1. κἀμοὶ (lemma: ἐγώ) -> gender: unknown; number: unknown; case: unknown
2. αὐτῷ (lemma: αὐτός) -> gender: unknown; number: unknown; case: unknown
3. ᾧ (lemma: ὅς) -> gender: unknown; number: unknown; case: unknown
4. σοι (lemma: σύ) -> gender: unknown; number: unknown; case: unknown
5. τούτῳ (lemma: οὗτος) -> gender: unknown; number: unknown; case: unknown

## 12. aorist_indicative_active_w
**Part of Speech Family:** verb
**Frequency:** 8510

---
topic: aorist, indicative, active (ω)
pos: verb
frequency: 8510
---

# Lesson: The Aorist – Indicative – Active Voice  

*(Target: beginner‑intermediate students of Ancient Greek)*  

---

## 1. What the Aorist Is  

The **aorist** is one of the three basic tenses of the Greek verb (present, aorist, perfect).  
It expresses a **simple, completed action** in the past, present, or future, without reference to its duration or repetition. In English it is often rendered by a simple past (“*he went*”, “*they saw*”) or by a perfect (“*he has gone*”) when the aorist is used with a future meaning.

The **indicative mood** is the “statement” mood – it is used for ordinary factual sentences.  

The **active voice** means the subject of the verb performs the action (as opposed to middle or passive).

So **aorist‑indicative‑active** = “a simple, completed action performed by the subject, stated as a fact”.

---

## 2. Two Main Types of Aorist  

Greek has **two morphological families** for the aorist:

| Type | Typical formation | Example verb | Meaning of the aorist |
|------|-------------------|--------------|-----------------------|
| **First‑aorist** (also called *regular* aorist) | Add **‑σ‑** (or **‑θ‑** for some verbs) to the verb stem, then attach the aorist endings. | λυ‑ (stem of *λύω* “to loose”) → **λυσ‑** → *ἔλυσα* “I loosed” | Simple past action |
| **Second‑aorist** (also called *strong* aorist) | No **‑σ‑**; the aorist stem is often a modified version of the present stem (often with a lengthened vowel, a different consonant, or a reduplication). | γι‑ (stem of *γίγνομαι* “to become”) → **ἐγένε‑** → *ἐγένετο* “he became” | Simple past action, often with a more “perfect‑like” nuance |

Both types share the **same set of active indicative endings** (see below).  

---

## 3. Active Indicative Aorist Endings  

| Person | Singular | Plural |
|--------|----------|--------|
| 1st | **‑α** (or **‑ον** after a vowel) | **‑αμεν** |
| 2nd | **‑ας** (or **‑ας** after a vowel) | **‑ατε** |
| 3rd | **‑ε(ν)** (or **‑ε** after a vowel) | **‑αν** |

> **Note:** The endings are the same for both first‑ and second‑aorist stems. The difference lies in the stem itself.

### 3.1. The “‑ω” Ending – a Quick Comparison  

The **present active indicative** uses the ending **‑ω** in the 1st‑person singular (e.g., *λύω* “I loose”).  
The aorist **does not** use **‑ω**; its 1st‑person singular ending is **‑α** (or **‑ον**).  
We include the present table here for contrast, because many students initially confuse the two.

| Tense | 1st‑sg. active indicative |
|-------|--------------------------|
| Present | **‑ω** (e.g., *λύω*) |
| Aorist  | **‑α** (e.g., *ἔλυσα*) |

---

## 4. Full Paradigms  

Below are complete active‑indicative aorist tables for a **regular first‑aorist** verb (*λύω* “to loose”) and a **second‑aorist** verb (*γίγνομαι* “to become”).  

### 4.1. First‑Aorist Active Indicative (λύω)  

| Person | Form | Transliteration | Gloss |
|--------|------|----------------|-------|
| 1st sg. | **ἔλυσα** | *élusa* | I loosed |
| 2nd sg. | **ἔλυσας** | *élusas* | you (sg.) loosed |
| 3rd sg. | **ἔλυσε(ν)** | *éluse* / *élusen* | he/she/it loosed |
| 1st pl. | **ἐλύσαμεν** | *elúsamen* | we loosed |
| 2nd pl. | **ἐλύσατε** | *elúsate* | you (pl.) loosed |
| 3rd pl. | **ἔλυσαν** | *élusan* | they loosed |

*The augment **ἐ‑** (or **ἔ‑**) is added to the stem in the aorist indicative to mark past time.*

### 4.2. Second‑Aorist Active Indicative (γίγνομαι)  

| Person | Form | Transliteration | Gloss |
|--------|------|----------------|-------|
| 1st sg. | **ἐγένετο** | *egéneto* | I became |
| 2nd sg. | **ἐγένεσθαι** (middle/passive) – *active* uses **ἐγένεσας**? Actually *γίγνομαι* is deponent; active aorist is rare. For illustration we use *ἔλαβον* (second‑aorist of *λαμβάνω*). | | |
| 3rd sg. | **ἔλαβεν** | *élaben* | he/she/it took |
| 1st pl. | **ἐλάβομεν** | *elábomen* | we took |
| 2nd pl. | **ἐλάβετε** | *elábete* | you (pl.) took |
| 3rd pl. | **ἔλαβον** | *élabon* | they took |

*(The verb *λαμβάνω* “to take” is a classic second‑aorist; its aorist stem is *λαβ‑*.)*

---

## 5. Key Rules & Common Exceptions  

| Rule | Explanation |
|------|-------------|
| **Augment** | In the indicative aorist (both first and second), a **temporal augment** is prefixed to the verb: **ἐ‑** before a consonant, **ἔ‑** before a vowel. This marks past time. |
| **Reduplication** | Some second‑aorist verbs show **reduplication** (e.g., *ἔδωκα* from *δίδωμι*). The reduplicated syllable is usually a short vowel + the same consonant (e.g., *ε‑*). |
| **Contract verbs** | Verbs whose stems end in a vowel (e.g., *φιλέω*) contract in the aorist: *ἔφιλον* → *ἔφιλον*? Actually first‑aorist of *φιλέω* is *ἔφιλσα* (rare). Many contract verbs have **second‑aorist** forms with **‑ε‑** (e.g., *ἔδωκα* from *δίδωμι*). |
| **Irregular stems** | Some verbs have irregular aorist stems: *εἰμί* → *ἦν* (imperfect), *ἔσομαι* (future), *ἦλθον* (from *ἔρχομαι*). These are memorised individually. |
| **Spurious diphthongs** | In the aorist, the diphthongs **ει** and **ου** can be “spurious” (i.e., they represent a long vowel, not a true diphthong). Example: *ἔδει* (it was necessary) from *δεῖ*. |
| **Middle‑passive forms** | The aorist also has middle and passive voices, but this lesson focuses on the active. Remember that many verbs are **deponent** (they have only middle/passive forms). |

---

## 6. Example Sentences  

| Greek (aorist, active, indicative) | Transliteration | English |
|-----------------------------------|----------------|---------|
| **ἔλυσα τὸν δεσμὸν.** | *élusa tòn desmòn.* | I loosed the bond. |
| **ἔλαβον τὰ δῶρα.** | *élabon tà dôra.* | They took the gifts. |
| **ἔγραψεν τὸν λόγον.** | *égrapsen tòn lógon.* | He wrote the word. |
| **ἐβούλεσθε ἰδεῖν τὸν πόλεμον.** | *ebóulesthe ideîn tòn pólemon.* | You (pl.) wanted to see the war. |
| **ἔσπευδον εἰς τὴν πόλιν.** | *éspeudon eis tḕn pólīn.* | I hurried to the city. |

*Notice the augment (ἐ‑) and the aorist endings.*

---

## 7. Usage & Context  

1. **Simple past actions** – The aorist is the default tense for a single, completed event:  
   *ἔφαγον* “I ate (once)”.  

2. **Narrative sequence** – In storytelling, aorist verbs often appear in succession to move the plot forward.  

3. **Future meaning** – When combined with particles like **ἄν** (potential) or **ὅπως**, the aorist can express a future action:  
   *ἔσται* (future) vs. *ἔσται* (aorist of *εἰμί* used for future in indirect speech).  

4. **Contrast with present** – The present indicates an ongoing or habitual action; the aorist indicates a punctual one.  
   *παιδεύω* “I am teaching” vs. *ἐπαίδευσα* “I taught (once)”.  

5. **Aorist of perception verbs** – Verbs of seeing, hearing, etc., often use the aorist to indicate a single perception: *ἔειδον* “I saw”.  

---

## 8. Historical Development & Etymology  

- The **aorist** derives from the Proto‑Indo‑European (PIE) **aorist suffix** *‑h₁‑* (a “perfective” marker). In Greek it developed into the **‑σ‑** (first aorist) and the **‑ε‑/‑ο‑** (second aorist) augmentations.  

- The **augment** (ἐ‑/ἔ‑) is a relic of the PIE **pre‑verbial augment** that marked past time in many Indo‑European languages (e.g., Sanskrit *a‑*).  

- The **first‑aorist** pattern (stem + σ) reflects a **suffixal formation** that became grammaticalized in Greek.  

- The **second‑aorist** preserves older **strong verb** patterns, where the aorist stem is often a **zero‑grade** or **lengthened grade** of the root, sometimes with reduplication (e.g., *ἔδωκα* from *δίδωμι*).  

- Over time, the aorist lost its original aspectual nuance (simple perfective) and became the **default past tense** in

What is the number and person of the marked verbs in each sentence?

1. " τὴν δ̓ ἀπαμειβόμενος προσέφη πολύμητις Ὀδυσσεύς. <u>βῆ</u> δ̓ ἰέναι, πολλαὶ δὲ μετεσσεύοντο γεραιαί.

2. " τὸν δ̓ ἀπαμειβόμενος προσέφη πολύμητις Ὀδυσσεύς · " γιγνώσκω, φρονέω · τά γε δὴ νοέοντι κελεύεις. ὣς ἔφατ̓ εὐχόμενος, τοῦ δ̓ <u>ἔκλυε</u> Φοῖβος Ἀπόλλων.

3. " τὴν δ̓ ἀπαμειβόμενος προσέφη πολύμητις Ὀδυσσεύς " μαῖα, τίη δὲ σὺ τὰς μυθήσεαι; ἐν δὲ δύω <u>ποίησε</u> πόλεις μερόπων ἀνθρώπων καλάς.

4. Ἱερώνυμος δ̓ ὁ περιπατητικὸς περισπουδάστους φησὶν γενέσθαι τοὺς τῶν παίδων ἔρωτας ὅτι πολλάκις ἡ τῶν νέων ἀκμὴ καὶ τὸ πρὸς ἀλλήλους ἑταιρικὸν συμφρονῆσαν πολλὰς τυραννίδας <u>καθεῖλεν</u>. Κολοφωνίους ἄνδρας στάσι ἑσσωθέντας καὶ ἐκπεσόντας ἐκ τῆς πατρίδος ὑπεδέξαντο. " τὸν δ̓ ἀπαμειβόμενος προσέφη πολύμητις Ὀδυσσεύς " τοιγὰρ ἐγώ τοι ταῦτα μάλ̓ ἀτρεκέως ἀγορεύσω. ὁ δὲ Βάρκας ὀψὲ μὲν συνῆκε τὴν ἐπίθεσιν τῶν ἐκ τῆς πόλεως διὰ τὴν ἀπόστασιν τῶν στρατοπέδων · οὐδὲ μὴν συνεὶς οὐδ̓ οὕτως <u>κατετάχει</u> πρὸς τὴν βοήθειαν διὰ τὰς μεταξὺ δυσχωρίας. ἠχὴ δ̓ ἀμφοτέρων ἵκετ̓ αἰθέρα καὶ Διὸς αὐγάς.

5. οἳ δ̓ ὡς οὖν εἴδονθ̓ ὅ τ̓ ἄῤ ἐκ Διὸς ἤλυθεν ὄρνις, μᾶλλον ἐπὶ Τρώεσσι <u>θόρον</u>, μνήσαντο δὲ χάρμης.

6. ὣς φάτο, τὸν δὲ πατὴρ ὀλοφύρατο δάκρυ χέοντα, <u>νεῦσε</u> δέ οἱ λαὸν σόον ἔμμεναι οὐ δ̓ ἀπολέσθαι.

7. νήποινοί κεν ἔπειτα δόμων ἔντοσθεν ὄλοισθε. ἣ δ̓ ἐκύει φίλον υἱόν, ὃ δ̓ ἕβδομος ἑστήκει μείς · ἐκ δ̓ <u>ἄγαγε</u> πρὸ φόως δὲ καὶ ἠλιτόμηνον ἐόντα, Ἀλκμήνης δ̓ <u>ἀπέπαυσε</u> τόκον, <u>σχέθε</u> δ̓ Εἰλειθυίας.

8. τοῦ δ̓ ὠρίνετο θυμὸς ἀκούοντος κακὰ ἔργα, <u>βῆ</u> δ̓ ἰέναι, χροῒ δ̓ ἔντἐ ἐδύσετο παμφανόωντα.

9. τίς τοι τάδε εἵματ̓ ἔδωκεν; οἳ δ̓ ἐλελίχθησαν καὶ ἐναντίοι ἔσταν Ἀχαιῶν · Ἀργεῖοι δ̓ <u>ὑπέμειναν</u> ἀολλέες οὐ δὲ φόβηθεν.

10. ὣς τὸ μὲν <u>ἐξετέλεσσε</u> καὶ οὐκ ἐθέλουσ̓, ὑπ̓ ἀνάγκης. ὣς φάτ̓ Ἀθηναίη, ὃ δ̓ ἐπείθετο, χαῖρε δὲ θυμῷ, στῆ δ̓ ἄῤ ἐπὶ μελίης χαλκογλώχινος ἐρεισθείς.

Find one finite verb in each sentence and give its dictionary lemma.

1. τὠυτὸ γὰρ ἀντιθήσω ἐκείνῳ, ὅτι νικήσας τοὺς ἀντιουμένους ἐλᾷς ἰθὺ τῆς ἀρχῆς τῆς Τομύριος. " τὸν δ̓ ἀπαμειβόμενος προσέφης, Εὔμαιε συβῶτα · " τοιγὰρ ἐγώ τοι, τέκνον, ἀληθέα πάντ̓ ἀγορεύσω. <u>δούπησεν</u> δὲ πεσών, τὸν δὲ σκότος ὄσσε <u>κάλυψεν</u>.

2. ἀλλ̓ ἄγε μοι τὸν ὄνειρον ὑπόκριναι καὶ ἄκουσον. οἳ δὲ τάχα προγένοντο, δύω δ̓ ἅμ̓ ἕποντο νομῆες τερπόμενοι σύριγξι · δόλον δ̓ οὔ τι <u>προνόησαν</u>.

3. οἱ δὲ προειρημένοι Χαλκιδεῖς παῤ αὑτοῖς φασιν ἁρπασθῆναι τὸν Γανυμήδην ὑπὸ τοῦ Διὸς καὶ τὸν τόπον δεικνύντες Ἁρπάγιον καλοῦσιν, ἐν ᾧ καὶ μυρρίναι διάφοροι πεφύκασιν. οὗτοι δὲ οἱ Αἰολέες χώρην μὲν <u>ἔτυχον</u> κτίσαντες ἀμείνω Ἰώνων, ὡρέων δὲ ἥκουσαν οὐκ ὁμοίως. τίνες ἔμμεναι εὐχετόωντο; οἱ δὲ περὶ τὸν Μάθω κατανοήσαντες τὸν Ἀννίβαν ῥᾳθύμως καὶ κατατεθαρρηκότως ἀναστρεφόμενον, ἐπιθέμενοι τῷ χάρακι πολλοὺς μὲν τῶν Καρχηδονίων <u>ἀπέκτειναν</u>, πάντας δ̓ <u>ἐξέβαλον</u> ἐκ τῆς στρατοπεδείας, <u>ἐκυρίευσαν</u> δὲ καὶ τῆς ἀποσκευῆς ἁπάσης, <u>ἔλαβον</u> δὲ καὶ τὸν στρατηγὸν Ἀννίβαν ζωγρίᾳ. ὣς ἄρα φωνήσας ἡγήσατο · τοὶ δ̓ ἅμ̓ ἕποντο ἠχῇ θεσπεσίῃ, ἐπὶ δ̓ ἴαχε λαὸς ὄπισθεν.

4. ὣς ὃ μὲν Αἰτωλοῖσιν ἀπήμυνεν κακὸν ἦμαρ εἴξας ᾧ θυμῷ · τῷ δ̓ οὐκέτι δῶρα <u>τέλεσσαν</u> πολλά τε καὶ χαρίεντα, κακὸν δ̓ ἤμυνε καὶ αὔτως.

5. ὣς ἔφαθ̓, αἳ δ̓ <u>ἐπέμυξαν</u> Ἀθηναίη τε καὶ Ἥρη · πλησίαι αἵ γ̓ ἥσθην, κακὰ δὲ Τρώεσσι μεδέσθην.

6. σμερδαλέον δὲ μέγ̓ <u>ᾤμωξεν</u>, περὶ δ̓ ἴαχε πέτρη, ἡμεῖς δὲ δείσαντες ἀπεσσύμεθ̓ · αὐτὰρ ὁ μοχλὸν <u>ἐξέρυσ̓</u> ὀφθαλμοῖο πεφυρμένον αἵματι πολλῷ. τοῦ δ̓ ἤτοι κλέος ἔσται ὅσον τ̓ ἐπικίδναται ἠώς · τοῦ δ̓ ἐπιλήσονται τὸ ἐγὼ καὶ Φοῖβος Ἀπόλλων ἥρῳ Λαομέδοντι <u>πολίσσαμεν</u> ἀθλήσαντε.

7. ἀθάνατος δὲ θεὸς τοτὲ μὲν προπάροιθ̓ Ὀδυσῆος φαίνετο θαρσύνων, τοτὲ δὲ μνηστῆρας ὀρίνων θῦνε κατὰ μέγαρον · τοὶ δ̓ ἀγχιστῖνοι ἔπιπτον. ὣς ἔφαθ̓, οἳ δ̓ ἄρα τοῦ μάλα μὲν <u>κλύον</u> ἠδὲ πίθοντο.

8. ὣς τὼ μὲν χαλεποῖσιν ἀμειβομένω ἐπέεσσιν ἕστασαν · οἱ δ̓ <u>ἀνόρουσαν</u> ἐυκνήμιδες Ἀχαιοὶ ἠχῇ θεσπεσίῃ, δίχα δέ σφισιν ἥνδανε βουλή. τοῖο δ̓ ἀπ̓ ὀφθαλμῶν χύτο δάκρυα χωομένοιο, οὕνεκα τὰς μὲν ὅρα ἔτι καὶ πολὺ μᾶλλον ἰούσας, οἳ δέ οἱ ἐβλάφθησαν ἄνευ κέντροιο θέοντες.

9. τελευτήσαντος δ̓ αὐτοῦ γηραιοῦ ἐν τῇ πατρίδι καὶ τῆς ἐκφορᾶς παρὰ τὴν θάλατταν γιγνομένης κατὰ τύχην ἐν τῇ Μιλήτῳ, ἐν τῷ λιμένι πλῆθος δελφίνων ἐφάνη ἐν τῇ ἡμέρᾳ ἐκείνῃ μικρὸν ἀπωτέρω τῶν συνεκκομιζόντων τὸν Κοίρανον, ὡσεὶ συνεκφερόντων καὶ συγκηδευόντων τὸν ἄνθρωπον. οὕτω δὴ τὸ δεύτερον Ἰωνίη ἐδεδούλωτο. " " ὣς εἰπὼν <u>ἀνόρουσε</u>, τίθει δ̓ ἄρα οἱ πυρὸς ἐγγὺς εὐνήν, ἐν δ̓ ὀΐων τε καὶ αἰγῶν δέρματ̓ ἔβαλλεν. τὸν δὲ δολοφρονέουσα προσηύδα πότνια Ἥρη · αἰνότατε Κρονίδη ποῖον τὸν μῦθον ἔειπες.

10. Μυρμιδόνων δ̓ ἐπί τε κλισίας καὶ νῆας ἱκέσθην, τὸν δ̓ <u>εὗρον</u> φρένα τερπόμενον φόρμιγγι λιγείῃ καλῇ δαιδαλέῃ, ἐπὶ δ̓ ἀργύρεον ζυγὸν ἦεν, τὴν ἄρετ̓ ἐξ ἐνάρων πόλιν Ἠετίωνος ὀλέσσας · τῇ ὅ γε θυμὸν ἔτερπεν, ἄειδε δ̓ ἄρα κλέα ἀνδρῶν.

## 13. present_participle_active_w
**Part of Speech Family:** verb
**Frequency:** 7608

---
topic: present, participle, active (ω)
pos: verb
frequency: 7608
---

# Lesson: The Present Active Participle (‑ω)  

*Target level: Beginner‑Intermediate*  
*Prerequisites: Greek alphabet, basic noun declension, present‑tense verb endings*  

---

## 1. What is the Present Active Participle?

The **present active participle** is a verbal adjective that expresses an **ongoing, simultaneous action** performed by the subject of the verb.  
- It is **active** (the subject does the action).  
- It is **present** (the action is happening at the same time as the main verb).  

In English it is often rendered with **‑ing** clauses or adjectives:

| Greek | English gloss |
|-------|---------------|
| γράφων | “writing” (while writing) |
| ἀκούων | “hearing” (as he hears) |
| λυουσά | “the one who is loosening” |

The participle **declines** like a regular adjective: it has gender, number, and case, and must agree with the noun it modifies.

---

## 2. Forming the Present Active Participle  

### 2.1. The Stem

1. **Take the present‑tense stem** of the verb (the part that appears before the personal endings ‑ω, ‑εις, ‑ει, …).  
2. **Add the participial suffix** **‑ων‑** (masc./neut.) or **‑ουσα‑** (fem.).  

The basic pattern is:

| Gender/Number | Suffix | Example (λύω “to loose”) |
|---------------|--------|--------------------------|
| Masculine Singular Nominative | ‑ων | λύων |
| Feminine Singular Nominative | ‑ουσα | λύουσα |
| Neuter Singular Nominative/Accusative | ‑ον | λύον |
| Masculine Plural Nominative | ‑οντες | λύοντες |
| Feminine Plural Nominative | ‑ουσαι | λύουσαι |
| Neuter Plural Nominative/Accusative | ‑οντα | λύοντα |

From this stem the full **adjective paradigm** is built by adding the regular case endings of a first‑/second‑declension adjective.

### 2.2. Full Declension Table (example with **λύων** “loosing”)

| Case | Masculine | Feminine | Neuter |
|------|-----------|----------|--------|
| **Singular** | | | |
| Nominative | λύων | λύουσα | λύον |
| Genitive | λύοντος | λύουσης | λύοντος |
| Dative | λύοντι | λύουσῃ | λύοντι |
| Accusative | λύοντα | λύουσαν | λύον |
| Vocative | λύων | λύουσα | λύον |
| **Plural** | | | |
| Nominative | λύοντες | λύουσαι | λύοντα |
| Genitive | λύοντων | λύουσῶν | λύοντων |
| Dative | λύουσι(ν) | λύουσῖν | λύουσι(ν) |
| Accusative | λύοντας | λύουσας | λύοντα |
| Vocative | λύοντες | λύουσαι | λύοντα |

> **Note:** The dative plural may appear with **‑σι(ν)** (older) or **‑σι** (later).  

### 2.3. Common Verb Classes & Their Particularities  

| Verb class | Present stem | Participle formation | Example |
|------------|--------------|----------------------|---------|
| **Regular –ω verbs** (e.g., *ποιέω*) | ποιε‑ | **‑ων / ‑ουσα / ‑ον** | ποιῶν, ποιουσα, ποιον |
| **Contract verbs –εω** (e.g., *φιλεῖν*) | φιλε‑ | **‑ων / ‑ουσα / ‑ον** (contract) | φιλῶν, φιλουσα, φιλον |
| **Contract verbs –οω** (e.g., *διδάσκειν*) | διδασκ‑ | **‑ων / ‑ουσα / ‑ον** (no extra contraction) | διδάσκων, διδάσκουσα, διδάσκον |
| **Verbs with a short vowel + ρ** (e.g., *βούλομαι* – deponent) | βουλ‑ | **‑ων / ‑ουσα / ‑ον** (same) | βούλων, βούλουσα, βούλον |
| **Irregular stems** (e.g., *εἰμί* “to be”) | — | No present active participle (instead use *ὤν* from *εἰμί*) | ὤν, οὖσα, ὄν |

**Key point:** The participle **always ends in ‑ων / ‑ουσα / ‑ον** regardless of the verb’s ending, but the stem may contract (e.g., *φιλε‑* → *φιλ‑*).

---

## 3. Key Rules & Common Exceptions  

| Rule | Explanation |
|------|-------------|
| **Agreement** | The participle must agree **in gender, number, and case** with the noun it modifies, just like any adjective. |
| **Position** | It can appear **before** or **after** the noun; placement often affects emphasis. |
| **Circumstantial use** | When the participle expresses a circumstance (e.g., “while doing X”), it is usually **in the same case as the governing verb’s subject** (often nominative). |
| **Temporal nuance** | The present active participle denotes **simultaneity** with the main verb, not future or past. |
| **No perfect‑active present participle** | The present active participle never expresses a completed action; for that we use the **aorist** or **perfect** participles. |
| **Irregularities** | • **εἰμί** → *ὤν, οὖσα, ὄν* (suppletive). <br>• **ἔχω** → *ἔχων, ἔχουσα, ἔχον* (stem *ἐχ‑*). |
| **Deponent verbs** | Deponent verbs (middle/passive in form, active in meaning) form a present active participle **identical** to the regular pattern (e.g., *βούλομαι* → *βούλων*). |
| **Contract verbs** | When the stem ends in *‑ε* or *‑ο* before *‑ω*, the participial suffix attaches after the contraction (e.g., *φιλε‑* → *φιλ‑* → *φιλῶν*). |

---

## 4. Example Sentences  

| Greek | Transliteration | English |
|-------|----------------|---------|
| **Ὁ ἀνὴρ τὸν λόγον γράφων ἐξέρχεται.** | Ho anēr ton logon graphōn exerchetai. | The man, **writing** the sentence, goes out. |
| **Ἡ γυνὴ τὴν ὁδὸν ἰδούσα ἔσπευδεν.** | Hē gynē tēn hodon idousa espeuden. | The woman, **seeing** the road, hurried. |
| **Τὰ παιδία τὰ ἐν τῇ κλίνῃ κλῶντα ἔπαιζον.** | Ta paidia ta en tē klinē klōnta epaizen. | The children, **lying** on the couch, were playing. |
| **Ὀδυσσεύς, Ἀχαιῶν ἡγεμών, Ἀργεῖον ἀνέχων, ἐπὶ τὴν νῆσον ἦλθεν.** | Odysseus, Akhaiōn hēgemōn, Argeion anechōn, epi tēn nēson ēlthen. | Odysseus, **leading** the Achaeans, came to the island. |

*Notice the participle agrees with its noun (masc. nom. sg. – γράφων, fem. nom. sg. – ἰδούσα, neut. nom./acc. pl. – κλῶντα).*

---

## 5. Usage & Context  

1. **Descriptive adjective** – Often used like any adjective to give a characteristic:  
   *ὁ **παιδεύων** διδάσκει* “the **educating** teacher teaches”.  

2. **Circumstantial clause** – Provides background information, usually translated with “while” or “when”:  
   *Ἀνὴρ **πλέων**, ἔπλευσεν* “The man, **while sailing**, set out.”  

3. **Supplementary (absolute) construction** – When the participle stands with a noun in a case other than the subject, it can form a **genitive absolute** (rare with present active, more common with aorist):  
   *Ἀνδρὸς **πλέοντος**, ἦλθον* “When the man was sailing, I came.”  

4. **Epithets in poetry** – Poets frequently use the present active participle as a vivid epithet:  
   *Ἀργεῖος **προπορεύων*** “the Argive **leading the way**”.  

5. **Agreement with abstract nouns** – The participle can modify abstract nouns, turning a verb phrase into a noun phrase:  
   *τὸ **παιδεύον** ἀγαθόν* “the **educating** good (thing)”.

---

## 6. Historical Development & Etymology  

| Aspect | Details |
|--------|---------|
| **Proto‑Indo‑European origin** | The participial suffix *‑ont‑* (present active) is inherited from PIE *‑ont‑*, which also gave Latin **‑ens** (e.g., *amans* “loving”). |
| **Greek phonological change** | PIE *‑ont‑* became Greek *‑ων* after the loss of the final *‑t* and the addition of the nasal *‑n*. The feminine *‑ουσα* reflects the earlier *‑ous‑a* formation. |
| **Old Greek** | Already present in Homeric Greek, though often with a more lexical (noun‑like) feel. Example: *ἄγων* “leading”. |
| **Classical period** | The participle became a fully grammaticalized adjective, used extensively in prose and poetry for both descriptive and circumstantial purposes. |
| **Later Greek** | The form persisted unchanged through Koine and Byzantine Greek, though the frequency of circumstantial use declined in favor of finite clauses. |
| **Etymology of the term** | *Participle* comes from Latin *participium* “a sharing, a part”. The Greek name **παράμετρον** (rare) was later replaced by the Latin term in modern scholarship. |

---

## 7. Quick Reference Summary  

| Feature | Present Active Participle (‑ω) |
|---------|------------------------------|
| **Meaning** | Ongoing, simultaneous action performed by the subject |
| **Form** | Stem + **‑ων / ‑ουσα / ‑ον** (masc./fem./neut.) |
| **Declension** | First/second‑declension adjective pattern |
| **Agreement** | Must match noun in gender, number, case |
| **Typical uses** | Descriptive adjective, circumstantial clause, poetic epithet |
| **Irregularities** | *εἰμί* → *ὤν, οὖσα, ὄν*; contract verbs contract before the suffix |
| **Historical note** | Direct descendant of PIE *‑ont‑*; attested from Homer onward |

---  

**End of Lesson**. Feel free to refer back to the tables when you encounter participles in reading; the pattern is regular once you know the verb’s present stem. Happy studying!

### Exercise Set 2

What is the number and person of the marked verbs in each sentence?

1. τῶν δὲ κατὰ τὠυτὸ αἱ γνῶμαι συνεξέπιπτον <u>κελευόντων</u> ἐσδέκεσθαι Τόμυρίν τε καὶ τὸν στρατὸν αὐτῆς ἐς τὴν χώρην. " ὣς φάθ̓, ὁ δ̓ αὖτις ἰὼν κατ̓ ἄῤ ἕζετο · τῷ δὲ συβώτης. οὐ δέ νυ σοί περ ἐντρέπεται φίλον ἦτορ ἀνεψιοῦ κταμένοιο;

2. ἣ δ̓ ἄτη σθεναρή τε καὶ ἀρτίπος, οὕνεκα πάσας πολλὸν ὑπεκπροθέει, φθάνει δέ τε πᾶσαν ἐπ̓ αἶαν <u>βλάπτουσ̓</u> ἀνθρώπους · αἳ δ̓ ἐξακέονται ὀπίσσω.

3. τοῖσι δ̓ ἔπειθ̓ ἥρως Αἰγύπτιος ἦρχ̓ ἀγορεύειν, ὃς δὴ γήραϊ κυφὸς ἔην καὶ μυρία ᾔδη. τῶν δ̓ αἳ μὲν λεπτὰς ὀθόνας ἔχον, οἳ δὲ χιτῶνας εἵατ̓ ἐϋννήτους, ἦκα <u>στίλβοντας</u> ἐλαίῳ · καί ῥ̓ αἳ μὲν καλὰς στεφάνας ἔχον, οἳ δὲ μαχαίρας εἶχον χρυσείας ἐξ ἀργυρέων τελαμώνων.

4. οἱ δὲ πανημέριοι σεῖον ζυγὸν ἀμφὶς <u>ἔχοντες</u>. ὣς ἔφαθ̓, οἳ δ̓ ἄρα τοῦ μάλα μὲν κλύον ἠδὲ πίθοντο, καί ῥ̓ ἀπομορξαμένω κονίην δύσαντο χιτῶνας.

5. " τὸν δ̓ ἀπαμειβόμενος προσέφη πολύμητις Ὀδυσσεύς · " γιγνώσκω, φρονέω · τά γε δὴ <u>νοέοντι</u> κελεύεις. ὣς ἔφατ̓ εὐχόμενος, τοῦ δ̓ ἔκλυε Φοῖβος Ἀπόλλων.

6. ὣς φάτο, τὸν δὲ πατὴρ ὀλοφύρατο δάκρυ <u>χέοντα</u>, νεῦσε δέ οἱ λαὸν σόον ἔμμεναι οὐ δ̓ ἀπολέσθαι.

7. τοῦ δ̓ ὠρίνετο θυμὸς <u>ἀκούοντος</u> κακὰ ἔργα, βῆ δ̓ ἰέναι, χροῒ δ̓ ἔντἐ ἐδύσετο παμφανόωντα.

8. ὣς τὸ μὲν ἐξετέλεσσε καὶ οὐκ <u>ἐθέλουσ̓</u>, ὑπ̓ ἀνάγκης. ὣς φάτ̓ Ἀθηναίη, ὃ δ̓ ἐπείθετο, χαῖρε δὲ θυμῷ, στῆ δ̓ ἄῤ ἐπὶ μελίης χαλκογλώχινος ἐρεισθείς.

9. ἄλλα δ̓ ἀριστήεσσι δίδου γέρα καὶ βασιλεῦσι · τοῖσι μὲν ἔμπεδα κεῖται, ἐμεῦ δ̓ ἀπὸ μούνου Ἀχαιῶν εἵλετ̓, ἔχει δ̓ ἄλοχον θυμαρέα · τῇ <u>παριαύων</u> τερπέσθω.

10. οἱ δὲ προειρημένοι Χαλκιδεῖς παῤ αὑτοῖς φασιν ἁρπασθῆναι τὸν Γανυμήδην ὑπὸ τοῦ Διὸς καὶ τὸν τόπον δεικνύντες Ἁρπάγιον καλοῦσιν, ἐν ᾧ καὶ μυρρίναι διάφοροι πεφύκασιν. οὗτοι δὲ οἱ Αἰολέες χώρην μὲν ἔτυχον κτίσαντες ἀμείνω Ἰώνων, ὡρέων δὲ <u>ἥκουσαν</u> οὐκ ὁμοίως. τίνες ἔμμεναι εὐχετόωντο; οἱ δὲ περὶ τὸν Μάθω κατανοήσαντες τὸν Ἀννίβαν ῥᾳθύμως καὶ κατατεθαρρηκότως ἀναστρεφόμενον, ἐπιθέμενοι τῷ χάρακι πολλοὺς μὲν τῶν Καρχηδονίων ἀπέκτειναν, πάντας δ̓ ἐξέβαλον ἐκ τῆς στρατοπεδείας, ἐκυρίευσαν δὲ καὶ τῆς ἀποσκευῆς ἁπάσης, ἔλαβον δὲ καὶ τὸν στρατηγὸν Ἀννίβαν ζωγρίᾳ. ὣς ἄρα φωνήσας ἡγήσατο · τοὶ δ̓ ἅμ̓ ἕποντο ἠχῇ θεσπεσίῃ, ἐπὶ δ̓ ἴαχε λαὸς ὄπισθεν.

### Exercise Set 3 (Verbs)

Find one finite verb in each sentence and give its dictionary lemma.

1. ἐπείτε δὲ ἐπεραιώθη τὸν Ἀράξεα, νυκτὸς ἐπελθούσης εἶδε ὄψιν <u>εὕδων</u> ἐν τῶν Μασσαγετέων τῇ χωρῇ τοιήνδε · ἐδόκεε ὁ Κῦρος ἐν τῷ ὕπνῳ <u>ὁρᾶν</u> τῶν Ὑστάσπεος παίδων τὸν πρεσβύτατον <u>ἔχοντα</u> ἐπὶ τῶν ὤμων πτέρυγας καὶ τουτέων τῇ μὲν τὴν Ἀσίην τῇ δὲ τὴν Εὐρώπην ἐπισκιάζειν. πρῆξαι δ̓ ἀργαλέον τι μετὰ πλεόνεσσιν ἐόντα ἄνδρα καὶ ἴφθιμον, ἐπεὶ ἦ πολὺ φέρτεροί εἰσι. μινυνθάδιος γὰρ ἔμελλεν ἔσσεσθ̓ · ἤδη γάρ οἱ ἐπόρνυε μόρσιμον ἦμαρ Παλλὰς Ἀθηναίη ὑπὸ Πηλεΐδαο βίηφιν.

2. οἳ δὲ μέγα <u>φρονέοντες</u> ἐπὶ πτολέμοιο γεφύρας εἴατο παννύχιοι, πυρὰ δέ σφισι καίετο πολλά.

3. ἀθάνατος δὲ θεὸς τοτὲ μὲν προπάροιθ̓ Ὀδυσῆος φαίνετο <u>θαρσύνων</u>, τοτὲ δὲ μνηστῆρας <u>ὀρίνων</u> θῦνε κατὰ μέγαρον · τοὶ δ̓ ἀγχιστῖνοι ἔπιπτον. ὣς ἔφαθ̓, οἳ δ̓ ἄρα τοῦ μάλα μὲν κλύον ἠδὲ πίθοντο.

4. ὣς τὼ μὲν χαλεποῖσιν ἀμειβομένω ἐπέεσσιν ἕστασαν · οἱ δ̓ ἀνόρουσαν ἐυκνήμιδες Ἀχαιοὶ ἠχῇ θεσπεσίῃ, δίχα δέ σφισιν ἥνδανε βουλή. τοῖο δ̓ ἀπ̓ ὀφθαλμῶν χύτο δάκρυα χωομένοιο, οὕνεκα τὰς μὲν ὅρα ἔτι καὶ πολὺ μᾶλλον ἰούσας, οἳ δέ οἱ ἐβλάφθησαν ἄνευ κέντροιο <u>θέοντες</u>.

5. τελευτήσαντος δ̓ αὐτοῦ γηραιοῦ ἐν τῇ πατρίδι καὶ τῆς ἐκφορᾶς παρὰ τὴν θάλατταν γιγνομένης κατὰ τύχην ἐν τῇ Μιλήτῳ, ἐν τῷ λιμένι πλῆθος δελφίνων ἐφάνη ἐν τῇ ἡμέρᾳ ἐκείνῃ μικρὸν ἀπωτέρω τῶν <u>συνεκκομιζόντων</u> τὸν Κοίρανον, ὡσεὶ <u>συνεκφερόντων</u> καὶ <u>συγκηδευόντων</u> τὸν ἄνθρωπον. οὕτω δὴ τὸ δεύτερον Ἰωνίη ἐδεδούλωτο. " " ὣς εἰπὼν ἀνόρουσε, τίθει δ̓ ἄρα οἱ πυρὸς ἐγγὺς εὐνήν, ἐν δ̓ ὀΐων τε καὶ αἰγῶν δέρματ̓ ἔβαλλεν. τὸν δὲ δολοφρονέουσα προσηύδα πότνια Ἥρη · αἰνότατε Κρονίδη ποῖον τὸν μῦθον ἔειπες.

6. ἤδη ὦν ἐν τῇ παροιχομένῃ νυκτὶ <u>εὕδων</u> εἶδον τῶν σῶν παίδων τὸν πρεσβύτατον <u>ἔχοντα</u> ἐπὶ τῶν ὤμων πτέρυγας καὶ τουτέων τῇ μὲν τὴν Ἀσίην τῇ δὲ τὴν Εὐρώπην ἐπισκιάζειν. " τὸν δ̓ αὖ Τηλέμαχος πεπνυμένος ἀντίον ηὔδα · " τοιγὰρ ἐγώ τοι, ξεῖνε, μάλ̓ ἀτρεκέως ἀγορεύσω. στρεφθεὶς γὰρ μετόπισθεν ἐν ἀσπίδος ἄντυγι πάλτο, τὴν αὐτὸς φορέεσκε ποδηνεκέ̓ ἕρκος ἀκόντων · τῇ ὅ γ̓ ἐνὶ βλαφθεὶς πέσεν ὕπτιος, ἀμφὶ δὲ πήληξ σμερδαλέον κονάβησε περὶ κροτάφοισι πεσόντος.

7. τοῦ δὲ Ποσειδάων μεγάλ̓ ἔκλυεν αὐδήσαντος · αὐτίκ̓ ἔπειτα τρίαιναν ἑλὼν χερσὶ στιβαρῇσιν ἤλασε Γυραίην πέτρην, ἀπὸ δ̓ ἔσχισεν αὐτήν · καὶ τὸ μὲν αὐτόθι μεῖνε, τὸ δὲ τρύφος ἔμπεσε πόντῳ, τῷ ῥ̓ Αἴας τὸ πρῶτον ἐφεζόμενος μέγ̓ ἀάσθη · τὸν δ̓ ἐφόρει κατὰ πόντον ἀπείρονα <u>κυμαίνοντα</u>. τοῦ γὰρ ἐγὼ θεράπων, μία δ̓ ἤγαγε νηῦς εὐεργής · Μυρμιδόνων δ̓ ἔξειμι, πατὴρ δέ μοί ἐστι Πολύκτωρ.

8. <u>κομῶντες</u> δὲ τὰς κεφαλὰς μίτρῃσι ἀναδέονται, μεμυρισμένοι πᾶν τὸ σῶμα. ἦ γὰρ ἔτ̓ εἰσὶ καὶ ἀφνειοὶ καλέονται. ὄφῤ οἳ τοὺς ἐνάριζον ἀπ̓ ἔντεα, τόφρα δ̓ Ἀχαιοὶ τάφρῳ καὶ σκολόπεσσιν ἐνιπλήξαντες ὀρυκτῇ ἔνθα καὶ ἔνθα φέβοντο, δύοντο δὲ τεῖχος ἀνάγκῃ.

9. τὸν δὲ μετ̓ Ἀτρεΐδαι Ἀγαμέμνων καὶ Μενέλαος, τοῖσι δ̓ ἐπ̓ Αἴαντες θοῦριν ἐπιειμένοι ἀλκήν, τοῖσι δ̓ ἐπ̓ Ἰδομενεὺς καὶ ὀπάων Ἰδομενῆος Μηριόνης ἀτάλαντος Ἐνυαλίῳ ἀνδρειφόντῃ, τοῖσι δ̓ ἐπ̓ Εὐρύπυλος Εὐαίμονος ἀγλαὸς υἱός · Τεῦκρος δ̓ εἴνατος ἦλθε παλίντονα τόξα <u>τιταίνων</u>, στῆ δ̓ ἄῤ ὑπ̓ Αἴαντος σάκεϊ Τελαμωνιάδαο.

10. ἔνεστι ἐπεὰν ὦν ἀπίκωνται <u>πλέοντες</u> ἐς τὴν Βαβυλῶνα καὶ διαθέωνται τὸν φόρτον, νομέας μὲν τοῦ πλοίου καὶ τὴν καλάμην πᾶσαν ἀπ̓ ὦν ἐκήρυξαν, τὰς δὲ διφθέρας ἐπισάξαντες ἐπὶ τοὺς ὄνους ἀπελαύνουσι ἐς τοὺς Ἀρμενίους. ἔσκε δὲ πατρὸς ἐμοῖο γυνὴ Φοίνισσ̓ ἐνὶ οἴκῳ, καλή τε μεγάλη τε καὶ ἀγλαὰ ἔργα ἰδυῖα · τὴν δ̓ ἄρα Φοίνικες πολυπαίπαλοι ἠπερόπευον. Ἕκτωρ μὲν Στιχίον τε καὶ Ἀρκεσίλαον ἔπεφνε, τὸν μὲν Βοιωτῶν ἡγήτορα χαλκοχιτώνων, τὸν δὲ Μενεσθῆος μεγαθύμου πιστὸν ἑταῖρον · Αἰνείας δὲ Μέδοντα καὶ Ἴασον ἐξενάριξεν.

## 14. imperfect_indicative_active_w
**Part of Speech Family:** verb
**Frequency:** 6485

---
topic: imperfect, indicative, active (ω)
pos: verb
frequency: 6485
---

# Lesson: The Imperfect – Indicative – Active (ω‑type)

**Target:** Beginner‑intermediate students of Ancient Greek  
**Focus:** How to form and use the imperfect indicative active for verbs of the **ω‑type** (the regular “present‑stem” verbs that end in **‑ω** in the present system).

---

## 1. What is the Imperfect?

| Term | Meaning in Greek | Rough English equivalent |
|------|------------------|--------------------------|
| **Imperfect** | A past‑time, **continuous** or **repeated** action. | “was doing”, “used to do”, “kept doing”. |
| **Indicative** | The ordinary mood of statement (as opposed to subjunctive, optative, etc.). |
| **Active** | The subject performs the action (as opposed to middle or passive). |

The imperfect therefore describes an action that was **in progress** or **habitual** in the past, without implying that it is finished.

> **Example (English):** “I was walking home.”  
> **Greek (imperfect):** ἔβαιον τὴν οἰκίαν.

---

## 2. The ω‑type Verb

A **ω‑type** verb has a present‑stem ending in **‑ω** (or **‑ο‑** after the augment).  
Typical examples:  

| Verb | Meaning | Present‑stem | Imperfect stem |
|------|---------|--------------|----------------|
| λύω | “to loose, release” | λυ‑ | λυ‑ |
| παίω | “to strike” | παι‑ | παι‑ |
| τίθημι (irregular) – not ω‑type | – | – | – |

In this lesson we will use **λῦω** (to loose) as our model verb.

---

## 3. Forming the Imperfect (Active, Indicative)

### 3.1 The Augment

- The imperfect **always** receives an **augment** at the beginning of the verb.
- For verbs whose first syllable begins with a vowel, the augment is **ε‑** (the *e‑augment*).  
  - If the vowel is long, the augment **replaces** it (e.g., *ἦν* from *εἰμί*).  
- For verbs that start with a consonant, the augment is **ε‑** placed before the first consonant.

### 3.2 The Endings

The imperfect active uses the **‑ον** series of endings (the same as the present, but with a long *‑ο‑* before the personal ending).  

| Person | Ending (after the stem) | Full form for λῦω |
|--------|------------------------|-------------------|
| 1st sg. | **‑ον** | **ἔλυον** |
| 2nd sg. | **‑ες** | **ἔλυσας** |
| 3rd sg. | **‑ε(ν)** | **ἔλυε(ν)** |
| 1st pl. | **‑ομεν** | **ἐλύομεν** |
| 2nd pl. | **‑ετε** | **ἐλύετε** |
| 3rd pl. | **‑ον** | **ἔλυον** |
| 1st/2nd dual* | **‑ετον / ‑ετον** | **ἔλυετον / ἔλυετον** |
| 3rd dual* | **‑ετον** | **ἔλυετον** |

\*The dual is rare in prose but appears in poetry and early Greek.

### 3.3 Full Paradigm (Active, Indicative, Imperfect)

|          | Singular | Dual | Plural |
|----------|----------|------|--------|
| **1st**  | ἔλυον   | ἔλυετον | ἐλύομεν |
| **2nd**  | ἔλυσας | ἔλυετον | ἐλύετε |
| **3rd**  | ἔλυε(ν) | ἔλυετον | ἔλυον |

> **Note:** The 3rd‑sg. ending **‑ε(ν)** may appear with or without **ν** in poetry; the **ν** is the normal prose form.

---

## 4. Key Rules & Common Exceptions

| Rule | Explanation | Example |
|------|-------------|---------|
| **A. Augment** | Add **ε‑** before the stem. If the stem begins with a vowel, the augment may replace a long vowel. | λῦ‑ → **ἔ**λυ‑ → ἔλυον |
| **B. Vowel contraction** | When the augment **ε‑** meets a preceding vowel, they may contract (e.g., *ε + ι → ει*). In the ω‑type this rarely creates a diphthong because the stem begins with a consonant. | — |
| **C. Lengthening of the thematic vowel** | The thematic vowel **‑ο‑** of the imperfect is long; it is written **‑ο‑** (not **‑ε‑**) before the personal endings. | ἐ‑λύ‑**ο**μεν |
| **D. Irregular verbs** | Some verbs have special imperfect stems: <br>• **εἰμί** → ἦν, ἦσθα, ἦν, ἦμεν, ἦτε, ἦσαν (no **‑ον** series). <br>• **ἔχω** → ἔεχον, ἔεχες, ἔεχε(ν), ἐεχόμεν, ἐεχετε, ἔεχον (the stem changes). | — |
| **E. Dual forms** | The dual uses **‑ετον** for all persons; it is largely literary. | ἔλυετον (you two were loosing) |
| **F. Spurious diphthongs** | In some verbs the stem ends in **‑ει‑** or **‑ου‑**; the imperfect still uses the **‑ον** endings (e.g., *φιλεῖν* → ἔφιλον). | — |

---

## 5. Example Sentences

| Greek (Imperfect) | Transliteration | English |
|-------------------|----------------|---------|
| 1. ἔλυον τὸν δεσμὸν ἡμέρας πολλὰς. | **éluon** tòn desmòn hēméras pollàs. | “I was loosening the bond for many days.” |
| 2. ἐλύομεν τὰς ἀγγέλας ἐν τῇ ἀγορᾷ. | **elúomen** tàs ángélas en têi agorâi. | “We were delivering the messages in the marketplace.” |
| 3. ἔλυσας τὸν πόλεμον ταχέως. | **élusas** tòn pólemon tachéōs. | “You (sg.) were ending the war quickly.” |
| 4. ἔλυε τὰ παιδία ὁ διδάσκαλος. | **élue** tà paidía ho didáskalo̱s. | “The teacher was freeing the children.” |

---

## 6. Usage & Context

1. **Narrative past** – The imperfect is the default past tense for background actions in stories, especially when a later **aorist** or **perfect** marks a specific event.  
   - *ἔλυον* (I was loosening) → background; *ἔλυσα* (I loosed) → completed action.

2. **Repeated / habitual actions** – When an action occurs repeatedly or habitually in the past, the imperfect is preferred.  
   - *ἔλυον τὰς θύρας ἑκάστην ἡμέραν* – “I used to open the doors every day.”

3. **Descriptive scenes** – In epic poetry and drama, the imperfect paints a vivid picture of ongoing activity.  
   - *ἔλυε τὸν ἥλιον ὁ Ἀπόλλων* – “Apollo was drawing the sun.”

4. **Contrast with other past tenses** –  
   - **Imperfect vs. Aorist:** *ἔλυον* (was loosening) vs. *ἔλυσα* (loosed).  
   - **Imperfect vs. Perfect:** *ἔλυον* (ongoing) vs. *λελύκα* (have loosed).

---

## 7. Historical Development & Etymology

- The **imperfect** goes back to Proto‑Indo‑European (PIE) *‑nt‑* and *‑s‑* series, expressing continuous past.  
- The **augment** (*e‑*) is a Greek innovation (also found in Sanskrit *a‑* augment) that marks past time. It likely originated as a preverb meaning “before” that became a grammatical marker.  
- The **‑ον** endings derive from the PIE *‑ont‑* suffix, which also gave the present‑active endings in Greek. The lengthening of the thematic vowel (‑ο‑) distinguishes the imperfect from the present.  
- The **dual** forms survive from an older Indo‑European dual number, preserved only in a few Greek constructions.

---

## 8. Quick Reference Sheet

| Person | Imperfect Active (ω‑type) | Transliteration |
|--------|---------------------------|-----------------|
| 1st sg. | ἔ + stem + **‑ον** | **é‑…‑on** |
| 2nd sg. | ἔ + stem + **‑ες** | **é‑…‑es** |
| 3rd sg. | ἔ + stem + **‑ε(ν)** | **é‑…‑e(n)** |
| 1st pl. | ἐ + stem + **‑ομεν** | **e‑…‑omen** |
| 2nd pl. | ἐ + stem + **‑ετε** | **e‑…‑ete** |
| 3rd pl. | ἔ + stem + **‑ον** | **é‑…‑on** |
| Dual (all) | ἔ + stem + **‑ετον** | **é‑…‑eton** |

*Stem* = present‑stem without the final **‑ω** (e.g., λυ‑ for λῦω).

---

**End of Lesson** – You now know how to form and use the imperfect indicative active for regular ω‑type verbs in Ancient Greek!

### Exercise Set 2

What is the number and person of the marked verbs in each sentence?

1. ὣς ἔφαθ̓, οἳ δ̓ ἄρα τοῦ μάλα μὲν <u>κλύον</u> ἠδὲ πίθοντο.

2. τῷ δ̓ <u>ἔχεν</u> Αὐτομέδων, <u>τάμνεν</u> δ̓ ἄρα δῖος Ἀχιλλεύς.

3. " ὣς ἔφατ̓ εὐχόμενος, τοῦ δ̓ <u>ἔκλυε</u> Παλλὰς Ἀθήνη. οἳ δ̓ ἄῤ ἔσαν δίδυμοι · ὃ μὲν ἔμπεδον <u>ἡνιόχευεν</u>, ἔμπεδον <u>ἡνιόχεὐ</u>, ὃ δ̓ ἄρα μάστιγι <u>κέλευεν</u>.

4. τῶν δὲ κατὰ τὠυτὸ αἱ γνῶμαι <u>συνεξέπιπτον</u> κελευόντων ἐσδέκεσθαι Τόμυρίν τε καὶ τὸν στρατὸν αὐτῆς ἐς τὴν χώρην. " ὣς φάθ̓, ὁ δ̓ αὖτις ἰὼν κατ̓ ἄῤ ἕζετο · τῷ δὲ συβώτης. οὐ δέ νυ σοί περ ἐντρέπεται φίλον ἦτορ ἀνεψιοῦ κταμένοιο;

5. οἱ μὲν <u>ἐκήρυσσον</u>, τοὶ δ̓ ἠγείροντο μάλ̓ ὦκα. οἳ δ̓ ἤτοι δακέειν μὲν <u>ἀπετρωπῶντο</u> λεόντων, ἱστάμενοι δὲ μάλ̓ ἐγγὺς <u>ὑλάκτεον</u> ἔκ τ̓ ἀλέοντο.

6. οἳ δ̓ ἐπ̓ ὀνείαθ̓ ἑτοῖμα προκείμενα χεῖρας <u>ἴαλλον</u>.

7. οἳ δ̓ ἐπ̓ ὀνείαθ̓ ἑτοῖμα προκείμενα χεῖρας <u>ἴαλλον</u>.

8. τοῖσι δ̓ ἔπειθ̓ ἥρως Αἰγύπτιος ἦρχ̓ ἀγορεύειν, ὃς δὴ γήραϊ κυφὸς ἔην καὶ μυρία ᾔδη. τῶν δ̓ αἳ μὲν λεπτὰς ὀθόνας <u>ἔχον</u>, οἳ δὲ χιτῶνας εἵατ̓ ἐϋννήτους, ἦκα στίλβοντας ἐλαίῳ · καί ῥ̓ αἳ μὲν καλὰς στεφάνας <u>ἔχον</u>, οἳ δὲ μαχαίρας <u>εἶχον</u> χρυσείας ἐξ ἀργυρέων τελαμώνων.

9. οἱ δὲ πανημέριοι <u>σεῖον</u> ζυγὸν ἀμφὶς ἔχοντες. ὣς ἔφαθ̓, οἳ δ̓ ἄρα τοῦ μάλα μὲν <u>κλύον</u> ἠδὲ πίθοντο, καί ῥ̓ ἀπομορξαμένω κονίην δύσαντο χιτῶνας.

10. νήποινοί κεν ἔπειτα δόμων ἔντοσθεν ὄλοισθε. ἣ δ̓ <u>ἐκύει</u> φίλον υἱόν, ὃ δ̓ ἕβδομος ἑστήκει μείς · ἐκ δ̓ ἄγαγε πρὸ φόως δὲ καὶ ἠλιτόμηνον ἐόντα, Ἀλκμήνης δ̓ ἀπέπαυσε τόκον, σχέθε δ̓ Εἰλειθυίας.

### Exercise Set 3 (Verbs)

Find one finite verb in each sentence and give its dictionary lemma.

1. " τὸν δ̓ ἀπαμειβόμενος προσέφης, Εὔμαιε συβῶτα · " καὶ λίην ἀνδρός γε κύων ὅδε τῆλε θανόντος. ὣς εἰπὼν ὃ μὲν <u>ἦρχ̓</u>, ὃ δ̓ ἅμ̓ ἕσπετο ἰσόθεος φώς.

2. ὣς τὸ μὲν ἐξετέλεσσε καὶ οὐκ ἐθέλουσ̓, ὑπ̓ ἀνάγκης. ὣς φάτ̓ Ἀθηναίη, ὃ δ̓ ἐπείθετο, <u>χαῖρε</u> δὲ θυμῷ, στῆ δ̓ ἄῤ ἐπὶ μελίης χαλκογλώχινος ἐρεισθείς.

3. τὴν μὲν γὰρ Ἕλληνὲς ναυτίλλονται πᾶσα καὶ ἡ ἔξω στηλέων θάλασσα ἡ Ἀτλαντὶς καλεομένη καὶ ἡ Ἐρυθρὴ μία ἐοῦσα τυγχάνει. οἱ δ̓ αἶψ̓ <u>εἴσβαινον</u> καὶ ἐπὶ κληῗσι <u>καθῖζον</u>. ὣς εἰπὼν <u>ὄτρυνε</u> μένος καὶ θυμὸν ἑκάστου.

4. αἱ δ̓ ἄμοτον τανύοντο, <u>φέρον</u> δ̓ ἐσθῆτα καὶ αὐτήν, οὐκ οἴην, ἅμα τῇ γε καὶ ἀμφίπολοι <u>κίον</u> ἄλλαι. ἀλλ̓ ἴθι ταῦτα δ̓ ὄπισθεν ἀρεσσόμεθ̓ εἴ τι κακὸν νῦν εἴρηται, τὰ δὲ πάντα θεοὶ μεταμώνια θεῖεν.

5. οἱ δὲ προειρημένοι Χαλκιδεῖς παῤ αὑτοῖς φασιν ἁρπασθῆναι τὸν Γανυμήδην ὑπὸ τοῦ Διὸς καὶ τὸν τόπον δεικνύντες Ἁρπάγιον καλοῦσιν, ἐν ᾧ καὶ μυρρίναι διάφοροι πεφύκασιν. οὗτοι δὲ οἱ Αἰολέες χώρην μὲν ἔτυχον κτίσαντες ἀμείνω Ἰώνων, ὡρέων δὲ ἥκουσαν οὐκ ὁμοίως. τίνες ἔμμεναι εὐχετόωντο; οἱ δὲ περὶ τὸν Μάθω κατανοήσαντες τὸν Ἀννίβαν ῥᾳθύμως καὶ κατατεθαρρηκότως ἀναστρεφόμενον, ἐπιθέμενοι τῷ χάρακι πολλοὺς μὲν τῶν Καρχηδονίων ἀπέκτειναν, πάντας δ̓ ἐξέβαλον ἐκ τῆς στρατοπεδείας, ἐκυρίευσαν δὲ καὶ τῆς ἀποσκευῆς ἁπάσης, ἔλαβον δὲ καὶ τὸν στρατηγὸν Ἀννίβαν ζωγρίᾳ. ὣς ἄρα φωνήσας ἡγήσατο · τοὶ δ̓ ἅμ̓ ἕποντο ἠχῇ θεσπεσίῃ, ἐπὶ δ̓ <u>ἴαχε</u> λαὸς ὄπισθεν.

6. ὣς ὃ μὲν Αἰτωλοῖσιν <u>ἀπήμυνεν</u> κακὸν ἦμαρ εἴξας ᾧ θυμῷ · τῷ δ̓ οὐκέτι δῶρα τέλεσσαν πολλά τε καὶ χαρίεντα, κακὸν δ̓ <u>ἤμυνε</u> καὶ αὔτως.

7. ἐπεὶ ὅς τις ἀνὴρ ἀγαθὸς καὶ ἐχέφρων τὴν αὐτοῦ φιλέει καὶ κήδεται, ὡς καὶ ἐγὼ τὴν ἐκ θυμοῦ <u>φίλεον</u> δουρικτητήν περ ἐοῦσαν.

8. ἐπείτε δὲ ἐπεραιώθη τὸν Ἀράξεα, νυκτὸς ἐπελθούσης εἶδε ὄψιν εὕδων ἐν τῶν Μασσαγετέων τῇ χωρῇ τοιήνδε · <u>ἐδόκεε</u> ὁ Κῦρος ἐν τῷ ὕπνῳ ὁρᾶν τῶν Ὑστάσπεος παίδων τὸν πρεσβύτατον ἔχοντα ἐπὶ τῶν ὤμων πτέρυγας καὶ τουτέων τῇ μὲν τὴν Ἀσίην τῇ δὲ τὴν Εὐρώπην ἐπισκιάζειν. πρῆξαι δ̓ ἀργαλέον τι μετὰ πλεόνεσσιν ἐόντα ἄνδρα καὶ ἴφθιμον, ἐπεὶ ἦ πολὺ φέρτεροί εἰσι. μινυνθάδιος γὰρ <u>ἔμελλεν</u> ἔσσεσθ̓ · ἤδη γάρ οἱ ἐπόρνυε μόρσιμον ἦμαρ Παλλὰς Ἀθηναίη ὑπὸ Πηλεΐδαο βίηφιν.

9. σμερδαλέον δὲ μέγ̓ ᾤμωξεν, περὶ δ̓ <u>ἴαχε</u> πέτρη, ἡμεῖς δὲ δείσαντες ἀπεσσύμεθ̓ · αὐτὰρ ὁ μοχλὸν ἐξέρυσ̓ ὀφθαλμοῖο πεφυρμένον αἵματι πολλῷ. τοῦ δ̓ ἤτοι κλέος ἔσται ὅσον τ̓ ἐπικίδναται ἠώς · τοῦ δ̓ ἐπιλήσονται τὸ ἐγὼ καὶ Φοῖβος Ἀπόλλων ἥρῳ Λαομέδοντι πολίσσαμεν ἀθλήσαντε.

10. " ὣς ἔφατ̓ Ἀντίνοος · ὁ δ̓ ἄῤ οὐκ ἐμπάζετο μύθων. καὶ τὰ μὲν ἂρ σχίζῃσιν ἀφύλλοισιν <u>κατέκαιον</u>, σπλάγχνα δ̓ ἄῤ ἀμπείραντες <u>ὑπείρεχον</u> Ἡφαίστοιο.

## 15. present_indicative_active_w
**Part of Speech Family:** verb
**Frequency:** 6058

---
topic: present, indicative, active (ω)
pos: verb
frequency: 6058
---

# Lesson: The Present‑Indicative‑Active (‑ω) in Ancient Greek  

*Target audience: beginner‑intermediate students who already know the Greek alphabet and basic noun declension.*  

---

## 1. What the Present‑Indicative‑Active Is  

| Term | Meaning |
|------|---------|
| **Present** | The action is happening **now** or habitually, or it expresses a timeless truth. |
| **Indicative** | The “statement” mood – used for ordinary factual or neutral statements (as opposed to subjunctive, optative, imperative, etc.). |
| **Active** | The subject **does** the action (as opposed to middle or passive). |
| **‑ω** | The **first‑person singular** ending of the present‑indicative‑active for most verbs. All other persons are built from this stem. |

Thus, the present‑indicative‑active is the “default” verb form you will meet most often in prose and poetry: *λέγω* “I say”, *γράφω* “I write”, *παιδεύω* “I educate”, etc.

---

## 2. Forms and Patterns  

Ancient Greek verbs fall into three major **conjugation classes** in the present system:

1. **Thematic (vowel‑stem) verbs** – stem ends in a vowel (‑α, ‑ε, ‑ο, ‑ι, ‑υ).  
2. **Contract verbs** – the vowel of the stem contracts with the personal ending.  
3. **A‑thematic (consonant‑stem) verbs** – stem ends in a consonant (often ‑ν, ‑ρ, ‑σ, ‑τ, ‑κ, ‑γ, ‑δ, ‑β, ‑μ, ‑λ).  

Below are the **regular paradigms** for each class.  Irregular verbs (e.g., *εἰμί*, *ἔρχομαι*, *ἵστημι*) are treated in the “Exceptions” section.

### 2.1 Thematic Verbs (e.g., **φιλέω** “to love”)  

| Person | Ending | Form | Gloss |
|--------|--------|------|-------|
| 1st sg. | ‑ω | **φιλέω** | I love |
| 2nd sg. | ‑εις | **φιλεῖς** | you love |
| 3rd sg. | ‑ει | **φιλεῖ** | he/she/it loves |
| 1st pl. | ‑ομεν | **φιλοῦμεν** | we love |
| 2nd pl. | ‑ετε | **φιλεῖτε** | you (pl.) love |
| 3rd pl. | ‑ουσι(ν) | **φιλοῦσι(ν)** | they love |

*Note:* The thematic vowel **ο** appears before the personal endings; in the 2nd sg. and 3rd sg. the **ει** is a contraction of **ε + ι** (or **ο + ι**).  

### 2.2 Contract Verbs  

Contract verbs have a stem ending in **α, ε, or ο** that merges with the ending. Three sub‑types:

| Sub‑type | Example | Stem | Present‑Indicative‑Active Forms |
|----------|---------|------|---------------------------------|
| **‑α‑** (α‑contract) | **πράττω** “to do, practice” (stem *πρα‑*) | *πρα‑* | 1sg **πράττω**, 2sg **πράττεις**, 3sg **πράττει**, 1pl **πράττομεν**, 2pl **πράττετε**, 3pl **πράττουσι(ν)** |
| **‑ε‑** (ε‑contract) | **δείκνυμι** → **δείκνῡμι** “to show” (stem *δείκνυ‑*) – actually a mixed case, but for pure ε‑contract: **τιμάω** “to honor” (stem *τιμα‑*) | *τιμα‑* | 1sg **τιμῶ**, 2sg **τιμᾷς**, 3sg **τιμᾷ**, 1pl **τιμῶμεν**, 2pl **τιμᾶτε**, 3pl **τιμῶσι(ν)** |
| **‑ο‑** (ο‑contract) | **βούλομαι** (middle) – for active: **βούλομαι** is middle; a pure active example: **προσαγορεύω** “to call” (stem *προσαγορε‑*) – actually a thematic verb. A classic o‑contract active is **γίγνομαι** (middle). For active we use **ἀγοράζω** (no contraction). The true o‑contract active is rare; most o‑contract verbs are middle/passive. |

*The most common contract pattern you will meet is the **α‑contract** (‑α‑ + ‑ω → ‑ω, ‑α + ‑εις → ‑εις, etc.).*  

### 2.3 A‑thematic Verbs (e.g., **ἔρχομαι** is middle; a true active a‑thematic: **πίνω** “to drink”)  

| Person | Ending | Form | Gloss |
|--------|--------|------|-------|
| 1sg | ‑ω | **πίνω** | I drink |
| 2sg | ‑εις | **πίνεις** | you drink |
| 3sg | ‑ει | **πίνει** | he/she/it drinks |
| 1pl | ‑ομεν | **πίνομεν** | we drink |
| 2pl | ‑ετε | **πίνετε** | you (pl.) drink |
| 3pl | ‑ουσι(ν) | **πίνουσι(ν)** | they drink |

The a‑thematic pattern is identical to the thematic pattern **except** that there is **no thematic vowel** before the endings; the stem ends directly in a consonant.

---

## 3. Key Rules & Common Exceptions  

| Rule | Explanation | Example |
|------|-------------|---------|
| **1. The 1st‑person singular always ends in ‑ω** | This is the “base” from which the other forms are built. | *γράφω* “I write” |
| **2. The 2nd‑sg. ending is ‑εις** (or ‑ᾷς/‑ᾷ for contract‑α) | The vowel before ‑εις may be long (‑ᾷ) after contraction. | *φιλεῖς* vs. *τιμᾷς* |
| **3. The 3rd‑sg. ending is ‑ει** (or ‑ᾷ after α‑contract) | Same vowel length rule as above. | *πράττει* vs. *τιμᾷ* |
| **4. The 1st‑pl. ending is ‑ομεν** | The thematic vowel (ο) appears only in thematic verbs; a‑thematic verbs have the same ending because the stem already ends in a consonant. | *γράφουμεν* (thematic) vs. *πίνουμεν* (a‑thematic) |
| **5. The 2nd‑pl. ending is ‑ετε** | No contraction occurs here. | *γράφετε* |
| **6. The 3rd‑pl. ending is ‑ουσι(ν)** (or ‑ουσι for contract‑α) | The final **ν** is optional in prose; it appears more often in poetry. | *γράφουσι(ν)* |
| **7. Contract verbs shorten the vowel before the ending** | α‑contract: ‑α + ‑ω → ‑ω, ‑α + ‑εις → ‑ᾷς, etc.  ε‑contract: ‑ε + ‑ω → ‑ῶ, ‑ε + ‑εις → ‑ῆς, etc. | *τιμῶ* (from *τιμα‑* + ‑ω) |
| **8. Verbs with a **‑σ‑** in the stem often insert **‑σ‑** before the ending in the 2nd sg. and 3rd pl.** | This is the “‑σ‑” augment for present? Actually present does not have augment; the **‑σ‑** appears in the 2nd sg. of many a‑thematic verbs (e.g., *ἔρχομαι* is middle). For active a‑thematic verbs, the **‑σ‑** appears in the 2nd sg. of some verbs like **ἔχω** → **ἔχεις** (but that is thematic). The rule is more relevant for **future**. So we skip. |
| **9. Irregular verbs** | Some of the most common verbs have unique present stems or endings. | *εἰμί* “I am”, *ἔχω* “I have”, *ἔρχομαι* (middle), *ὁράω* “I see” (contract‑ο) |
| **10. The “‑ν” in 3rd‑pl. is often omitted in poetry** | Poets drop the **ν** for metrical reasons. | *γράφουσι* vs. *γράφουσιν* |

### 3.1 Irregular Verbs Worth Knowing  

| Verb | Present‑Indicative‑Active (1sg.) | Paradigm (selected) | Note |
|------|--------------------------------|---------------------|------|
| **εἰμί** “to be” | **εἰμί** | 1sg εἰμί, 2sg εἶ, 3sg ἐστί(ν), 1pl ἐσμέν, 2pl ἐστέ, 3pl εἰσίν | Suppletive stem; irregular forms. |
| **ἔχω** “to have” | **ἔχω** | 1sg ἔχω, 2sg ἔχεις, 3sg ἔχει, 1pl ἔχομεν, 2pl ἔχετε, 3pl ἔχουσι(ν) | The stem ends in **χ**, but the endings are regular. |
| **ὁράω** “to see” (ο‑contract) | **ὁρῶ** | 1sg ὁρῶ, 2sg ὁρᾷς, 3sg ὁρᾷ, 1pl ὁρῶμεν, 2pl ὁρᾶτε, 3pl ὁρῶσι(ν) | The long **ω** comes from contraction of **ο + ω**. |
| **δίδωμι** “to give” (mixed) | **δίδωμι** | 1sg δίδωμι, 2sg δίδως, 3sg δίδωσι(ν), 1pl διδόμεν, 2pl διδόμετε, 3pl διδόασι(ν) | Shows a mixture of a‑thematic and thematic patterns. |
| **ἔρχομαι** “to come” (middle) – not active, but appears often in texts. | — | — | Use the middle paradigm; not covered here. |

---

## 4. Example Sentences  

| Greek (present‑indicative‑active) | Transliteration | English |
|-----------------------------------|----------------|---------|
| **Λέγω τὸν νόμον.** | Légō tòn nómón. | I speak the law. |
| **Φιλεῖς τὸν φίλον σου.** | Phileîs tòn phílon sou. | You love your friend. |
| **Πίνουσιν οἶνον ἐν τῇ ἀγορᾷ.** | Pínousin oînón en têi agorâi. | They drink wine in the market. |
| **Τιμῶ τὸν πατέρα μου.** | Timô tòn patéra mou. | I honor my father. |
| **Ἐγὼ ἔχω τὰ βιβλία.** | Egṓ ékhō tà bíblia. | I have the books. |
| **Ὁ ἀνήρ ὁρᾷ τὸν οὐρανὸν.** | Ho anḗr ho̱râi tòn ouranòn. | The man sees the sky. |

*Notice the verb endings:* **-ω**, **-εις**, **-ει**, **-ομεν**, **-ετε**, **-ουσι(ν)**.

---

## 5. Usage & Context  

1. **Narrative prose** – The present‑indicative‑active is the default tense for describing actions that are happening **as the story is told** (e.g., *Ἀλέξανδρος ἰσχύει* “Alexander is strong”).  
2. **Historical present** – In historiography, the present is often used to make past events feel immediate (*Ἀθῆναι ἐπὶ τῇ μάχῃ νικῶσι* “Athens wins the battle”).  
3. **General truths & scientific statements** – Present expresses timeless facts (*ὁ ἥλιος ἀνατέλλει* “the sun rises”).  
4. **Habitual

8. ἐπεὶ ὅς τις ἀνὴρ ἀγαθὸς καὶ ἐχέφρων τὴν αὐτοῦ <u>φιλέει</u> καὶ κήδεται, ὡς καὶ ἐγὼ τὴν ἐκ θυμοῦ φίλεον δουρικτητήν περ ἐοῦσαν.

9. τοὶ δ̓ ἐξ ἀγροῖο πόλινδε ὠτρύνοντ̓ Ὀδυσεύς τ̓ ἰέναι καὶ δῖος ὑφορβός. ἀνὴρ δ̓ ὤριστος ὄλωλε Σαρπηδὼν Διὸς υἱός · ὃ δ̓ οὐ οὗ παιδὸς <u>ἀμύνει</u>.

Τρῶας δ̓ αὖθ̓ ἑτέρωθεν ἐκόσμει φαίδιμος Ἕκτωρ.

## 16. aorist_participle_active_w
**Part of Speech Family:** verb
**Frequency:** 5121

---
topic: aorist, participle, active (ω)
pos: verb
frequency: 5121
---

# Lesson: The Aorist Active Participle (‑ων, ‑ουσα, ‑ον)

---

## 1. What is the Aorist Active Participle?

The **aorist active participle** is a non‑finite verb form that:

* **Shows the action as a completed event** (aorist aspect) rather than an ongoing one (present) or a repeated/habitual one (imperfect).
* **Acts like an adjective**: it agrees with a noun in gender, number, and case.
* **Retains the active voice**, i.e., the subject of the participle is the doer of the action.

In English it is often rendered with a **‑ing** or **‑ed** clause, or with a simple past participle used adjectivally:

* *λόγος γράψας* – “the man **who wrote** …”  
* *τὰ δένδρα πεπτωκέντα* – “the trees **that have fallen**” (note: this is a perfect participle; the aorist would be *πεσόντα* “that fell”).

The aorist active participle is therefore a **“completed‑action adjective.”** It can be used:

* **Attributively** (directly before or after a noun).  
* **Predicatively** with a copular verb (εἰμί, γίγνομαι, γέγονα, etc.).  
* **Circumstantially** (as a subordinate clause) to indicate cause, time, condition, concession, etc.

---

## 2. Formation (Paradigm)

### 2.1. Basic Morphology

|                     | Masculine | Feminine | Neuter |
|---------------------|-----------|----------|--------|
| **Singular**        | ‑ων       | ‑ουσα    | ‑ον    |
| **Plural**          | ‑οντες    | ‑ουσαι   | ‑οντα  |

The participle is built from the **aorist active stem** + the **suffix ‑σ‑** (or directly ‑ν‑ for some verbs) + the appropriate **adjectival ending**.

**General pattern:**  

```
aorist‑active‑stem + σ + (masc. ‑ων / fem. ‑ουσα / neut. ‑ον)   →  singular
aorist‑active‑stem + σ + (masc. ‑οντες / fem. ‑ουσαι / neut. ‑οντα) → plural
```

### 2.2. Full Declension Table (example verb **γράφω** “to write”)

| Case / Number | Masculine Singular | Feminine Singular | Neuter Singular | Masculine Plural | Feminine Plural | Neuter Plural |
|---------------|--------------------|-------------------|-----------------|------------------|-----------------|---------------|
| **Nominative** | γράψας            | γράψασα           | γράψαν          | γράψαντες        | γράψασαι        | γράψαντα      |
| **Genitive**   | γράψαντος         | γράψασας          | γράψαντος       | γράψαντων        | γράψασῶν        | γράψαντων     |
| **Dative**     | γράψαντι          | γράψασῃ           | γράψαντι        | γράψασιν         | γράψασι(ν)      | γράψασιν      |
| **Accusative** | γράψαντα          | γράψασαν          | γράψαν         | γράψαντας        | γράψασας        | γράψαντα      |
| **Vocative**   | — (rare)          | —                 | —               | —                | —               | —             |

> **Note:** The aorist active participle is rarely used in the vocative; when needed, the nominative form is used.

### 2.3. Irregularities & Special Stems

| Verb type | Stem for aorist active | Participial form |
|-----------|------------------------|------------------|
| **‑μι verbs** (e.g., *τίθημι*) | aorist stem *ἔθηκ‑* | *ἔθηκ‑* + ‑σ‑ → *ἔθηκ‑* (no ‑σ‑) → *ἔθηκ‑* + endings: *ἔθηκ‑* (masc. ‑ων) → *ἔθηκ‑*?* (rare) |
| **Contract verbs** (e.g., *φιλέω*) | aorist stem *ἔφιλ‑* | *ἔφιλ‑* + ‑σ‑ → *ἔφιλ‑* + endings: *ἔφιλ‑* (masc. ‑ων) → *ἔφιλ‑*?* (→ *ἔφιλ‑*?*). In practice the participle is **ἔφιλ‑** + endings: *ἔφιλ‑* (masc. ‑ων) → *ἔφιλ‑*?* (→ *ἔφιλ‑*?*). |
| **Verbs with a‑stem** (e.g., *ἔρχομαι* – middle) | not applicable (no aorist active) | — |
| **Verbs whose aorist stem ends in ‑ν** (e.g., *διδάσκω* → aorist *ἐδίδαξα*) | aorist stem *διδάξ‑* | *διδάξ‑* + ‑σ‑ → *διδάξ‑* (the ‑σ‑ is often omitted) → *διδάξ‑* + endings: *διδάξ‑* (masc. ‑ων) → *διδάξ‑*?* → *διδάξ‑*?* (→ *διδάξ‑*?*). In practice we get **διδάξας** (masc. sg). |

> **Practical tip:** For most regular verbs the pattern **stem‑σ‑** + endings works without difficulty. When you encounter a verb that seems irregular, consult a dictionary for the aorist active participle form.

---

## 3. Key Rules & Common Exceptions

| Rule | Explanation |
|------|-------------|
| **Agreement** | The participle must match the noun it modifies in **gender, number, and case**. |
| **Aspect** | The aorist participle denotes a **single, completed action** that is prior to or simultaneous with the main verb, depending on context. |
| **Voice** | Active participles always have the **subject as the agent** of the action. |
| **Position** | It can appear **before** the noun (especially in poetry) or **after** it (more common in prose). |
| **With the verb *εἰμί*** | When used predicatively, the participle often takes the **nominative** (subject) case: *ὁ ἀνὴρ γράψας ἐστὶ σοφός* – “the man who wrote is wise.” |
| **With verbs of perception, knowledge, or speech** | The aorist participle frequently follows verbs like *ὁρῶ, λέγω, φημί*: *ὁρῶ τὸν ἀνθρώπον γράψαντα* – “I see the man who wrote.” |
| **Temporal vs. Causal use** | As a **temporal** clause it can mean “when/after”: *ἔλθων ὁ ἄνθρωπος* – “when the man came.” As a **causal** clause it can mean “because”: *παιδεύσας, ἐγένετο σοφός* – “having been educated, he became wise.” |
| **Exception – verbs with a‑stem** | Verbs whose aorist active stem ends in **‑α** (e.g., *πράσσω* → aorist *ἔπραξα*) form the participle **without the extra ‑σ‑**: *πράξας* (masc. sg). |
| **Exception – contract verbs** | For verbs whose aorist stem ends in a vowel, the **‑σ‑** may be dropped or merged: *ἔφη* → *ἔφη* (no participle). Such verbs simply lack an aorist active participle. |
| **Exception – verbs with *‑μι* (present) but aorist *‑σα* (e.g., *τίθημι* → *ἔθηκα*)** | The participle is formed from the aorist stem *ἔθηκ‑*: *ἔθηκας* (masc. sg). |

---

## 4. Example Sentences

| Greek (with transliteration) | English translation |
|------------------------------|---------------------|
| **1.** Ὁ ἀνὴρ **γράψας** τὸν λόγον ἀπῆλθεν.<br>*(Ho anēr **grapsas** ton logon apēlthen.)* | “The man **who wrote** the speech left.” |
| **2.** Ἡ γυνὴ **παιδεύσασα** τὸν παῖδα ἐγένετο εὐγενής.<br>*(Hē gynē **paideusas** ton paida egeneto eugenēs.)* | “The woman **who educated** the child became noble.” |
| **3.** Ἐγὼ **ἔλυσα** τὸν δεσμὸν καὶ ἀπῆλθον.<br>*(Ego **elusa** ton desmon kai apēlthon.)* – Here **ἔλυσα** is a finite aorist, but a participial version would be **λῦσας**: *λῦσας τὸν δεσμὸν, ἀπῆλθον* – “Having **loosened** the bond, I went away.” |
| **4.** Ὁ στρατηγὸς **προῆλθεν** τὴν πόλιν, **ἰδὼν** τὸν ἐχθρὸν ἐξέπνευσε.<br>*(Ho stratēgos **proēlthen** tēn polin, **idōn** ton echthon exepneuse.)* – Note the **present** participle **ἰδὼν** (aorist active participle of *ὁράω* is **ἰδὼν**, showing a completed seeing). |
| **5.** Ἀκούων τὸν λόγον, ὁ ἀκούων **ἔγραψεν** τὴν ἀπάντησιν.<br>*(Akouōn ton logon, ho akouōn **egrapsen** tēn apantēsin.)* – The participle **ἀκούων** (present) modifies the subject; the aorist active participle would be **ἀκούσας**: *ἀκούσας τὸν λόγον, ἔγραψεν…* – “Having **heard** the speech, he wrote the answer.” |

---

## 5. Usage & Contextual Notes

1. **Temporal Sequence** – The aorist participle often **precedes** the main verb in time:  
   *ἔλθων ὁ ἄνθρωπος, ἔλαβον τὸν δῶρον.* – “When the man **came**, I took the gift.”

2. **Causal Meaning** – It can express cause, especially with verbs of **saying, thinking, feeling**:  
   *Ἀγνοῶν τὸν νόμον, ἔπραξα τὸ ἀδίκημα.* – “Not knowing the law, I committed the crime.”

3. **Conditional / Concessive** – In poetry, the

### Exercises

### Exercise Set 1
